Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
12 min
Proof of Qiyas from the Mutawatir Practice of the Companions
Establishing that Sahaba used qiyas as a mutawatir practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul principle of tawatur ma'nawi to prove the validity of qiyas as a source of law from the practice of the Companions.

Core Idea
Mass transmission of the Sahaba's analogical reasoning, despite isolated chains, establishes qiyas as a certain source.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut addresses a key objection against qiyas: that reports of Companions using it are isolated (ahad) and thus not certain. The Hanafi response is that the common meaning—their practice of qiyas—is mutawatir in meaning (tawatur ma'nawi), producing certain knowledge. We will break down this argument and see how it refutes the doubters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested claim
Opponents of qiyas argue that the reports of Sahaba using analogical reasoning are ahad, hence not reliable for establishing a certain proof. They also claim that the reports might have hidden texts or that the analogies were specific to certain cases.
These objections are mentioned in the text: 'we do not accept that any Companion made analogies…'
2
Understand the Hanafi response: tawatur ma'nawi
The Hanafi scholar responds that although each report is individually ahad, the common theme—that the Companions regularly issued fatwas by qiyas—is transmitted by so many reports that it becomes mutawatir in meaning (tawatur ma'nawi). This yields certain knowledge.
The author states: 'the common factor among them—namely, the fatwa by qiyas—is mutawatir.'
3
Distinguish tawatur lafzi vs. ma'nawi
Tawatur lafzi requires exact wording across all chains; tawatur ma'nawi only requires a common meaning. The Hanafis accept the latter here, while the Mutakallimun (like in al-Mahsul) demand lafzi tawatur and thus reject the argument.
The text criticizes al-Mahsul for missing this point: 'the total number of transmitters is ten or twenty and tawatur is not achieved…'
4
Recognize the role of circumstantial evidence (qara'in)
The author adds that besides the reports, natural necessity (al-darura al-'adiyya) dictates that if the Companions had a text (nass), they would have cited it publicly. The absence of such texts in these cases confirms that they relied on qiyas.
Denying this is described as 'stubbornness' (mukabarah).
5
Evaluate the response to al-Mahsul's objection
Al-Mahsul (al-Razi) argued that a handful of reporters cannot produce tawatur. The Hanafi reply is that tawatur here is not about the number of chains per incident but the cumulative recurrence of the same type of action across many incidents, resulting in certain knowledge.
The passage concludes: 'there is no need for the answer that the matter is conjectural and practical…'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأصل الرابع/ القياس الغصنين؟ أصاحبه الذي خرج منه أم الشجرة، وقال زيد بن ثابت : لو أن جدولاً انبعث منه ساقية ثم انبعث من الساقية ساقيتان أيهما أقرب إحدى الساقيتين إلى صاحبتها أم الجدول؟ ومقصودهما توريث الأخ مع الجدّ قياساً على توريث العصبات الآخرين بجامع القرب في القرابة والشجرة والجدول تمثيل لقرب القرابة، لا أنه القياس حتى يرد عليه أنه ليس من القياس المتنازع فيه وصح عن ابن عباس أنه أرسل إلى زيد بن ثابت وقال: ألا يتقي الله زيد يجعل ابن الابن ابناً ولا يجعل أباً الأب أباً، فانظر تشديده حين مخالفته، هذا القياس فافهم (وذلك) أي الاحتجاج بالقياس أكثر كما روي (في المطولات من كتب السير) اعلم أنه كان في هذا الدليل شبه لأولي التلبيس، قد أشير إلى اندفاع بعضها. ونحن نذكر جلها مع فمنها لا نسلم أن أحداً من الصحابة قاس وما نقلتم أخبار آحاد لا تفيد القطع فيجوز عدم الصحة، ومنها : أن ما نقلتم عنهم لا تدل دلالة واضحة على كون فتواهم بالقياس، بل يجوز أن يكون عندهم نصوص جلية أو خفية لم يذكروها ومنها أنه سلمنا أن فتواهم للقياس لكن لأقيسة جزئية من نوع ما، فلا تدل على صحة الاستدلال الأقيسة، والجواب عنها أن بجميع المنقولات وإن كانت كل واحد واحد منها أخبار آحاد إلا أن القدر المشترك بينها وهو الفتوى بالقياس، وكون عادتهم ذلك متواتر يحدث العلم به بكثرة مطالعة أقضيتهم وتواريخهم، وعلم أيضاً بتكرر عملهم بالأقيسة أنه لم يكن بخصوص نوع أو فرد وعلم أيضاً بقرائن قاطعة للناقلين أنه لم يكن عندهم نص وأيضاً : الضرورة العادية قاضية بأنه لو كان عندهم نص استدلوا به في فتاويهم لأظهروا ، وإنكار هذا مكابرة، وما نقلنا عنهم وقائع متعدّدة تمثيلاً فلا يضر عدم دلالة البعض على كونها بالقياس، وإلى هذا كله أشار بقوله : تواتر، وبهذا ظهر لك فساد ما في «المحصول أن الغاية أن النقلة عشرة أو عشرون ولا يحصل بهم التواتر فلا يثبت به هذه المسألة القطعية ولا حاجة إلى ما أجاب به أن المسألة ظنية عملية يكفي فيها الظن.
The fourth principle: Qiyas. The two branches? Its originator? The one who derived from it or the tree? And Zaid ibn Thabit said: If a canal from which a stream branches, then from the stream two streams branch, which is closer to its companion: one of the two streams or the canal? And their purpose is to make the brother inherit with the grandfather by analogy to the inheritance of other inheritors due to the commonality of closeness in kinship. The tree and the canal are a representation of closeness of kinship, not that it is qiyas such that it could be objected that it is not the disputed qiyas. And it is authentically reported from Ibn Abbas that he sent to Zaid ibn Thabit and said: Does Zaid not fear Allah? He makes the son's son a son, but does not make the father's father a father. Look at his severity when he opposed this qiyas, so understand. (That is) i.e., the argument by qiyas is more, as reported (in the lengthy books of biographies). Know that in this proof there was a resemblance of confusion for some, and we have indicated the repulsion of some of them. And we will mention most of them along with: Among them: we do not accept that any of the Companions made analogies, and what you have transmitted are isolated reports that do not produce certainty, so they could be invalid. And among them: What you have transmitted from them does not clearly indicate that their fatwas were by qiyas; rather, it is possible that they had clear or hidden texts that they did not mention. And among them: Assuming that their fatwas were by qiyas, they were for particular analogies of a certain type, so they do not indicate the validity of analogical reasoning in general. And the answer to them: All the transmitted reports, although each individual one is an isolated report, the common factor among them—namely, the fatwa by qiyas and that their custom was that—is mutawatir. Knowledge of it is produced by frequent examination of their judgments and histories. It is also known by the repetition of their use of analogies that it was not specific to a type or individual. It is also known by definitive circumstantial evidence that they had no text. Moreover, natural necessity dictates that if they had had a text, they would have used it in their fatwas and manifested it. Denying this is stubbornness. What we have transmitted from them are multiple incidents as examples, so the lack of indication of some being by qiyas does no harm. And to all this he pointed by saying: 'mutawatir.' And by this the corruption of what is in 'al-Mahsul' is clear: that the total number of transmitters is ten or twenty and tawatur is not achieved through them, so this decisive matter is not established, and there is no need for the answer that the matter is conjectural and practical, and conjecture suffices in it.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut is an expansion on the fourth principle (al-qiyas) and its proof from the practice of the Companions. The author begins by citing examples from Zaid ibn Thabit and Ibn Abbas to demonstrate that the Companions did employ qiyas. Zaid's example uses a canal and streams to illustrate degrees of kinship in inheritance, while Ibn Abbas criticizes Zaid for inconsistency in applying qiyas. The author then addresses several objections raised by opponents of qiyas. The first set of objections denies that any Companion used qiyas, claiming that the transmitted reports are isolated (ahad) and thus not reliable for certainty. The author responds that although individual reports are ahad, the common theme—that the Companions regularly issued fatwas based on qiyas—is established through tawatur (mass transmission) due to the sheer volume of such reports and the historical record. He argues that the constant practice of the Companions, combined with the absence of any text (nass) in these cases, proves that qiyas was their method. The author then criticizes al-Mahsul's objection that the number of transmitters is too small for tawatur, asserting that the tawatur here is not about the chain but about the common meaning. This part of the text is a classic Hanafi defense of qiyas, relying on the cumulative evidence of the Companions' practice rather than individual proofs.

Key Terms
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning used by the Sahaba and sanctioned as a valid source of law.
تواتر (tawatur): Mass transmission of a common meaning across multiple individual reports, producing certain knowledge.
تواتر معنوي (tawatur ma'nawi): Tawatur based on a common meaning derived from multiple reports, even if the exact wording differs.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how does the Hanafi author refute the objection that the reports of Sahaba using qiyas are ahad and thus not certain?
A) He argues that each report is individually mutawatir.
B) He claims that the common meaning (al-fatawa bil qiyas) across reports is mutawatir.
C) He admits the point and says qiyas is established by ijma' instead.
D) He cites a Qur'anic verse that commands qiyas.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school proves the validity of qiyas as a certain source of law through the tawatur ma'nawi of the Companions' practice, despite individual reports being ahad.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate

Defending Qiyas: Refuting Ijma and Sahaba Objections
Defending Qiyas via rebuttals of Ijma and Sahaba objections

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and evaluate the Hanafi responses to two key objections against qiyas: the impossibility of ijma on qiyas and the Sahabas' criticism of ra'y.

Core Idea
The Companions' practice of qiyas is mutawatir in meaning; isolated statements against ra'y refer to ungrounded opinion.

This lesson examines how Hanafi usul scholars defend the validity of qiyas against two powerful objections. First, it addresses the claim that we cannot prove the Companions agreed on using qiyas because they never formally gathered and declared consensus. Second, it confronts explicit statements from senior Companions—Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali, Uthman, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Umar—that appear to condemn opinion (ra'y) and analogy. The Hanafi response reconciles these reports with the overwhelming evidence that the Companions themselves routinely employed analogical reasoning in deriving legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the first objection
The opponent argues that ijma on qiyas is impossible because the Companions did not gather in one assembly and speak unanimously. The passage refutes this by noting that knowledge of their agreement can be derived from circumstantial evidence (qara'in al-ahwal) and their actual practice.
The key point is that formal verbal agreement is not the only way to establish ijma.
2
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal of the ijma objection
The Hanafi reply: even without a formal gathering, we can be certain that the Companions did not retract from using qiyas. Their sudden consensus to fight the zakat refusers based on analogy is a clear example of their agreement through action.
This shows that circumstantial evidence can provide certainty (ilm) of their consensus.
3
Examine the second objection: Sahaba statements
The opponent cites statements from six senior Companions that appear to condemn ra'y and qiyas. The passage lists each statement: from Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali, Uthman, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Umar.
These statements are used by opponents to argue that qiyas is rejected by the very generation that established Islamic law.
4
Apply the Hanafi interpretation to each statement
The Hanafi response interprets each statement contextually: Abu Bakr's about Quran interpretation; Umar's warns against those who cling to opinion over Sunnah; Ali and Uthman's denies that religion originates from opinion; Ibn Mas'ud's is for non-mujtahids; Ibn Umar's says opinion is not Sunnah, not that it is invalid.
Thus, none of these statements reject valid qiyas; they only condemn ungrounded speculation.
5
Synthesize the overall Hanafi defense
The combined response: these reports are to be interpreted to reconcile them with the mutawatir practice of the Companions and Tabi'un in using qiyas. Therefore, qiyas remains a valid proof, and the objections are refuted.
This approach exemplifies the Hanafi principle of tawfiq (reconciliation) between conflicting evidences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
غير سلمنا أن الكل راضون به لكن يجوز أن لا يكون رضا البعض قبل رجوع الآخر، فلا يثبت الإجماع، وهذا لأن الكل لم يجتمعوا في محفل واحد ولم يتكلموا معاً. وقد مر جوابه في الأصل الثالث من أنهم وإن لم يتكلموا دفعة لكن حصل العلم بقرائن الأحوال أنهم، لم يرجعوا وأيضاً لم تم لزم بطلان الإجماع مطلقاً، وما في المحصول» أن الصحابة كانوا معدودين في أول الزمان فيمكن الاجتماع في محفل والتكلم معاً، ففيه أن المقصود لو تم لدل على بطلان تحقق الإجماع فيما تحقق قطعاً لأنه لم يتفق اجتماع المجتمعين في الحوادث الإجماعية بأن يتكلموا مع أن ههنا أيضاً وقع الاتفاق على قتال مانعي الزكاة بالقياس بغتة حين خرجوا له فتأمل ومنها : أنا سلمنا أنه وقع اتفاق الصحابة على العمل على مقتضى أقيستهم، لكن لا يلزم . منه عملنا على موجب أقيستنا بل يجوز أن يكونوا مختصين بهذا لكونهم من أفضل الأمة، وكون أذهانهم ثاقبة من أذهاننا وعقولهم متوقدة بنور إلهي، فإصابة الحق برأيهم أكثر وأقوى من إصابتنا فجواز تعبدهم بالقياس لا يوجب جواز تعبدنا به والجواب أنه لا شك في فضل آرائهم على آرائنا وفي كون إصابتهم للحق أكثر، لكن تعبدهم بالقياس لم يكن لاختصاصهم به، بل تلك الوقائع دلت على أن تعبدهم به لكونه حجة لا غير، ونحن وهم رضوان الله عليهم سيان في اتباع الحجج على أن من بعدهم من التابعين أيضاً قاسوا من نكير، فلا وجه للاختصاص أصلاً فافهم وتثبت وعورض بأن أجلة الصحابة ذموه) والمذموم منهم لا يكون حجة. ويمكن أن يحرر نقضاً أيضاً على الاستدلال بالإجماع (فعن) أفضل البشر بعد الأنبياء سيد الصدّيقين بعدهم أبي بكر الصديق رضي الله تعالى عنه حين سئل عن أتي سماء تظلني وأتي أرض تقلني لو قلت في كتاب الله برأيي وهذا ليس من الباب في شيء، فإنه إنما نفى القول بالرأي في تفسير كتاب الله تعالى لا أنه أنكر الرأي والقياس مطلقاً (وعن) أمير المؤمنين (عمر) رضي الله عنه (إياكم وأصحاب الرأي فإنهم أعداء السنن) وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه لا ذم فيه إلا لأصحاب الرأي والمتبادر منه من هو ملازم للرأي، ولا يلتفت إلى غيره كأصحاب النار، وهذا لا ينفي قياس صاحب السنن» (وعن أميري المؤمنين (علي وعثمان : لو كان الدين بالرأي لكان باطن الخف أولى المسح من ظاهره وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه إنما ينفي كون الدين ناشئاً عن الرأي، وهو كذلك، لأن وضع حكم ديني ابتداء لا بالرأي أصلاً، ولا يلزم منه نفي استعمال الرأي في مماثل لما ثبت من الدين ليعرف الحكم به (وعن ابن مسعود : إذا قلتم في دينكم بالقياس أحللتم كثيراً مما حرمه الله وحرمتم كثيراً مما أحل (الله) وهذا إنما يتم لو كان الخطاب للكل، وهو خفي بعد بل لعله لقوم ما وصلوا إلى درجة الاجتهاد بالقياس (وعن ابن عمر السنة ما سنه الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم وآله وأصحاب (وسلم، لا تجعلوا الرأي سنة للمسلمين) وهذا لو تم فإنما يدل على أن الرأي ليس سنة، لا أنه ليس حجة (الجواب أنه أي المنقول محمول على تصحيحه فيما لا يصح كالملغي الاعتبار والمصالح المرسلة وتقديمه على ما يقدح فيه من الكتاب والسنة (توفيقاً) بين هذه الروايات وبين ما تواتر عنهم من العمل بالرأي واستدل بما تواتر معناه وإن كانت التفاصيل آحاداً (من ذكره عليه) ، يصح الكلالة
But we concede that all are pleased with it, yet it is possible that some were not pleased before the others retracted, so consensus is not established. This is because all did not gather in one assembly nor speak together. Its answer has already passed in the third principle: that even if they did not speak all at once, knowledge is obtained through circumstantial evidence that they did not retract. And also, if not, then nullification of consensus would follow absolutely. And what is in al-Mahsul: 'The Companions were few in the beginning, so it is possible to gather in one assembly and speak together.' So in it, if the intent were fulfilled, it would indicate the nullification of the occurrence of consensus in what is definitely established, because it did not happen that the gatherers gathered in consensual incidents by speaking, even though here too agreement occurred on fighting the zakat refusers by analogy suddenly when they went out for it. So reflect. And among them: We concede that the Companions agreed to act according to their analogies, but our acting according to our analogies does not necessarily follow; rather, they may be specific to this due to being the best of the ummah, their minds more penetrating than ours, and their intellects kindled with divine light. So hitting the truth with their opinion is more and stronger than our hitting it. Thus, permissibility of their being bound by analogy does not necessitate permissibility of our being bound by it. The answer: There is no doubt about the superiority of their opinions over ours and their hitting the truth more, but their being bound by analogy was not due to their specificity; rather, those incidents indicated that they were bound by it because it is a proof and nothing else. We and they (may Allah be pleased with them) are equal in following proofs, especially since those after them from the Tabi'un also analogized without disapprobation, so there is no basis for specificity at all. So understand and be firm. And it was objected that the senior Companions disparaged it, and what is disparaged cannot be a proof. And it is possible to formulate a refutation also against the inference by consensus: (From) the best of humanity after the prophets, the chief of the truthful after them, Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be exalted with him), when he was asked, 'Which sky would shelter me and which earth would carry me if I said in the Book of Allah with my opinion?' This is not related at all, for he only negated speech with opinion in interpreting the Book of Allah, not that he denied opinion and analogy absolutely. (And from) the Commander of the Faithful, Umar (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Beware of the people of opinion, for they are enemies of the Sunnahs.' And you are not unaware that there is no blame in it except for the people of opinion, and the apparent meaning is the one who clings to opinion, and no attention is paid to others like the people of fire, and this does not negate the analogy of the person of the Sunnah. (And from) the two Commanders of the Faithful, Ali and Uthman: 'If religion were by opinion, then the inside of the sock would be more deserving of wiping than its outside.' And you are not unaware that it only negates religion arising from opinion, and it is so, because placing a religious ruling initially is not by opinion at all, and it does not necessitate negating the use of opinion in what is similar to what is established from religion to know the ruling by it. (And from) Ibn Mas'ud: 'If you speak in your religion by analogy, you would permit much of what Allah has forbidden and forbid much of what Allah has permitted.' This is only valid if the address is to everyone, and it is obscure, and perhaps it is for people who have not reached the level of ijtihad by analogy. (And from) Ibn Umar: 'The Sunnah is what the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings upon him and his family and companions) prescribed, do not make opinion a Sunnah for Muslims.' If valid, it only indicates that opinion is not Sunnah, not that it is not a proof. The answer: That which is transmitted is carried upon its correction in what is not valid, like the invalid consideration and the unregulated interests, and giving it precedence over what from the Book and Sunnah contradicts it, as a reconciliation between these reports and what is mutawatir from them of acting by opinion. And he argued with what is mutawatir in meaning, even if the details are ahad (from what is mentioned about it). It is valid for the kalala.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage is a dispute (usul_dispute) defending qiyas against two types of objections. First, it refutes the claim that ijma' (consensus) of the Companions on qiyas is impossible because they did not gather and agree verbally. The author replies that knowledge of their agreement can be derived from circumstantial evidence, and their actual practice—like the consensus on fighting zakat refusers based on analogy—shows they did use qiyas. Second, it addresses the objection that senior Companions like Abu Bakr, Umar, Ali, Uthman, Ibn Mas'ud, and Ibn Umar criticized opinion (ra'y) and qiyas. The author explains each report, showing they only criticized ungrounded opinion in interpreting the Quran or elevating opinion above the Sunnah, not the legitimate use of qiyas as a proof. The Hanafi position is that these reports are to be interpreted in a way consistent with the overwhelming evidence that the Companions themselves practiced qiyas. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as this is a core usul argument.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning: applying a ruling from an original case (aṣl) to a new case (farʿ) due to a shared effective cause (ʿilla).
الإجماع (al-ijmāʿ): Consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah on a legal ruling after the Prophet's era.
الرأي (ar-ra'y): Personal opinion or reasoning, often used pejoratively for ungrounded speculation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response in this passage, what was the real target of Umar's warning 'Beware of the people of opinion'?
A) Anyone who uses qiyas
B) Those who cling to opinion over the Sunnah
C) The Tabi'un who disagreed with the Companions
D) Followers of the Mu'tazila

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi defense of qiyas relies on interpreting isolated Sahaba statements in light of their mutawatir practice of analogical reasoning.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Textual ʿIlla Necessitates Generalized Ruling
Stating the Hanafi position that explicit 'illa in text requires generalization

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that an explicit textual cause (ʿilla manṣūṣa) requires extending the ruling to all instances where that cause exists, and evaluate the objection by Abu Abdullah al-Basri.

Core Idea
Explicit cause in text = general ruling, even without Qiyas.

This passage from 'Fawatih al-Rahamut' presents one of the foundational rules of Hanafi usul: when the Lawgiver explicitly mentions a reason (ʿilla) for a ruling, that ruling applies to every case where that reason is present. The author argues that this is understood directly from language, independent of formal qiyas. We will walk through the proofs and consider a key disagreement from Abu Abdullah al-Basri.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Central Issue
Read the heading: 'النص على العلة يكفي في إيجاب تعدية الحكم'. What is the claim? The claim is that an explicit textual cause is sufficient to extend the ruling to all similar cases.
This is a dispute within usul al-fiqh about the scope of ta'diyah.
2
Understand the Hanafi Proofs
The text gives three proofs: (1) linguistic understanding (doctor example), (2) avoiding arbitrariness (tahakkum), (3) the wine example. Identify each and note how they support the rule.
Proof (1) is based on 'urf (customary usage).
3
Examine the Objections and Responses
The author presents two objections: the Quran as sufficient explanation, and a hadith warning against qiyas. How does the Hanafi response neutralize them?
The Quran is general; the hadith is reinterpreted.
4
Analyze the Dispute with Abu Abdullah al-Basri
Al-Basri restricts the rule to prohibitions. What is his apparent basis? Why do Hanafis reject this limitation?
The thamarah al-khilaf: obligations vs. prohibitions.
5
Apply the Rule to New Cases
Using the principle, predict the ruling for other cases where a cause is explicit, such as the hadith about the cat ('إنها من الطوافين') or the prohibition of hand-dipping after waking.
Test your understanding by considering the scope.

(أقول: والحل) لدليلهم أن المنع فيه عن التسوية بين الثلاثة (والتخيير) في العمل (لا مطلقاً) عن نفس العمل بالقياس. وأيضاً يحتمل أن يكون المراد النهي عن التفريق في العمل في بعض الأحيان بواحد وفي زمان آخر بآخر، وفي زمان بآخر، فهم أي المفرّقون ،ضلوا، وإنما الواجب عليهم اتباع الحجج كلها في زمان واحد فافهم وتأمل. هذه الأمة مطلقاً · · · ، (مسألة : النص على العلة يكفي في إيجاب تعدية (الحكم في محال تحققها (ولو عدم التعبد بالقياس مطلقاً عند الحنفية و الإمام أحمد وأبي إسحق الشيرازي) الشافعي (وهو المختار، وعليه النظام، لكنه قال إنه منصوص) باستعمال الكلام فيه عرفاً أو لغة (وعند أبي عبدالله البصري المعتزلي يجب التعدية (في التحريم فقط خلافاً للجمهور) من أهل المذاهب لنا أولاً : إن ذكر العلة مع الحكم يفيد تعميمه في محال وجودها، لأنه المتبادر إلى الفهم) من هذا النحو من القرآن (كقول الطبيب لا تأكله لبرودته يفهم منه كل واحد نهيه عن البارد من غیر نظر وفكر، ولا يحتاج في الفهم إلى المعرفة بشرع القياس (و) لنا (ثانياً: لو لم يعم الحكم بل يخص في المنصوص لزم التحكم لأن الظاهر من التعليل (استقلالها) فتخلف الحكم مع وجود العلة المستقلة في بعض المحال دون بعض تحكم صريح، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن غاية ما لزم من هذا البيان ثبوت الحكم في موارد العلة لا ثبوته مع قطع النظر عن شرع القياس فإنه لو تم لزم عمومه في المنصوصة والمستنبطة جميعاً فافهم. (و) لنا (ثالثاً : حرمت الخمر لأنها مسكرة، في معنى علة الحرمة حقيقة الإسكار عرفاً، فإذا فهم المناظر عرفاً لزم تعميم الحكم أيضاً عرفا (وأما القول بأن حرمة الخمر معلل بالإسكار المنسوب إليه (لا)
The fourth principle: Qiyas. And peace and blessings upon him and his family and companions. The causes (ʿilal) for rulings, like: 'Do you see if there was a debt on your father?' [indicating] lifting the parts of a man's hajj from his father; 'Does the ripe date decrease when dry?' in answer to one who asked about selling fresh dates for dry dates; 'Indeed they (martyrs of Uhud) will be gathered' in the cause of burying martyrs without washing; 'It is among those that go around (the households)' in the cause of the purity of the leftover of a cat; 'For he does not know where his hand spent the night' in the cause of prohibiting a woken person from dipping his hand into the vessel; 'Perhaps the water helped kill it' in the cause of prohibiting what is killed by a trained dog when it is thrown into water. It was said in objection: If this proof is complete (for the textually stated cause, it is not complete for others). And in it is an indication that it is not complete in that also, because it is possible to mention causes as explanation of wisdom, not for qiyas. So reflect on it, for there is reflection in it. I say: It is not far to say in repelling it: Whoever knows from his habit that he explains with rational causes knows that he corrects the path absolutely, for it produces necessary knowledge through experience and repetition that rulings are caused by interests (as in experimental sciences). So reflect. The deniers said: First: Allah said: 'And We have sent down to you the Book as an explanation of everything' (al-Nahl:89) and similar; so nothing remains to be explained by qiyas so that it could be a proof in it. We said: Yes, it is an explanation, but in summary, because detailing everything in it is non-existent, so it is detailed by ijtihad and qiyas. Second: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him and his family and companions) said: 'You will act for a period by the Book, for a period by the Sunnah, and for a period by qiyas; if they do that, they have gone astray.' We said: It is rebutted by its like, for it would necessitate that the Book and Sunnah are also not proofs. Understand. I say: The solution to their proof is that the prohibition in it is about equating the three and choosing in action, not absolutely about acting by qiyas. Also, it may mean the prohibition of differentiating in action: sometimes by one, at another time by another, and at another time by another; i.e., those who differentiate go astray. Rather, the duty is to follow all proofs at one time. Reflect and ponder. This ummah absolutely . . . (Issue: The textual indication of the cause is sufficient to necessitate the extension of the ruling to instances where it exists, even if one does not adhere to qiyas at all, according to the Hanafis, Imam Ahmad, and Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi; al-Shafi'i (and it is the chosen view, upon it is al-Nizam, but he said it is textually explicit) by using the word in it customarily or linguistically. According to Abu Abdullah al-Basri al-Mu'tazili, it necessitates extension only in prohibition, contrary to the majority of scholars of the schools. For us: First, mentioning the cause with the ruling benefits its generalization in the instances of its existence, because it is readily understood from this type of Qur'an, like a doctor's saying: 'Do not eat it because of its coldness'; each person understands from it the prohibition of the cold without reflection or thought, and does not need knowledge of the law of qiyas to understand. Second: If the ruling were not general but specific to the text, then it would be arbitrariness, because the apparent meaning of the cause is its independence; thus, the absence of the ruling in some instances despite the existence of the independent cause is clear arbitrariness. And you are not unaware that the utmost required from this explanation is the establishment of the ruling in the instances of the cause, not its establishment irrespective of the law of qiyas. For if it were complete, its generality would apply to both textually stated and inferred causes. Understand. Third: Wine is prohibited because it is intoxicating; the meaning of the cause of prohibition is the reality of intoxication customarily. So when the interlocutor understands customarily, it necessitates generalizing the ruling also customarily. And as for the statement that the prohibition of wine is caused by intoxicating attributed to it (not).
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a rule (usul_rule) stating the Hanafi position that when the Lawgiver explicitly mentions a cause (ʿilla) for a ruling, that ruling applies to all cases where the cause is found, even if one does not accept qiyas as a source of law. The author first lists examples from hadith where the Prophet (s) gave causes (e.g., the cat's leftover is pure because it 'goes around' households; the prohibition of dipping hands after waking because one does not know where the hand was). These show that the Companions understood the cause as general. Then the passage addresses objections: (1) that the Quran is sufficient explanation, answered that it is general and requires ijtihad; (2) a hadith warning against acting by qiyas, reinterpreted as warning against choosing between sources rather than using all. Finally, the mas'ala: Hanafis, Ahmad, and Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi hold that textual 'illa suffices for ta'diyah; al-Shafi'i also holds it but calls it 'mansus'. Abu Abdullah al-Basri restricts it to prohibitions. Three proofs: (a) linguistic understanding from familiar contexts (doctor's advice), (b) neglect of cause would be arbitrary, (c) the example of wine being prohibited for intoxication—anything intoxicating is prohibited. The authority weight is from Zahir al-Riwayah as it reflects the established Hanafi principle.

Key Terms
العلة المنصوصة (al-ʿilla al-manṣūṣa): A cause for a ruling that is explicitly stated in the Quran or Hadith.
تعدية الحكم (taʿdiyat al-ḥukm): Extending the ruling from the original case to other cases where the same cause exists.
التحكم (al-taḥakkum): Arbitrariness or unjustified differentiation in legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in the passage, what is the primary reason that mentioning a cause (ʿilla) in the text obligates extending the ruling?
A) Because qiyas is a valid source of law
B) Because it is the readily understood linguistic meaning
C) Because the Companions practiced it
D) Because Imam Abu Hanifa said so

Key Takeaway
Explicit mention of a cause in a legal text necessitates extending the ruling to all instances of that cause, regardless of whether qiyas is accepted as a source.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Explicit 'Illa Obligates Extension of Ruling
Dispute on the binding force of an explicit 'illa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi argument that an explicit 'illa necessitates extension of the ruling, and critically evaluate the objections raised against it.

Core Idea
Explicit cause in a text compels extension—no qiyas needed.

When the Lawgiver explicitly states a cause for a ruling, does that automatically extend the ruling to all similar cases? The Hanafis, along with Imam Ahmad and others, argue yes: the plain linguistic understanding and logical consistency demand it. Their opponents, including some Mu'tazila, restrict extension to prohibitions only or require a separate proof for qiyas. This lesson dissects the arguments and counterarguments, revealing the deeper principles of Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Dispute
What exactly is being debated? Is the issue about the necessity of qiyas for extending rulings, or about the effect of an explicit cause stated in the very same text?
The dispute is not about qiyas in general; it is about the binding force of a cause mentioned in the text itself.
2
State the Hanafi Position and Its Three Proofs
The Hanafis hold that extension is obligatory even without recognizing qiyas as a proof. They present three proofs: (1) the doctor analogy – linguistic common understanding; (2) the arbitrary nature of specificity; (3) the wine example – customary understanding of cause.
Focus on how each proof relies on linguistic custom and logical reasoning.
3
Examine the Opponents' Objections
The opponents raise two main objections: (1) There is no explicit command or report obligating extension; (2) It would lead to absurdities like freeing all black slaves if someone says 'I freed Ghanim for his blackness.'
Understand the basis of each objection: lack of textual order and implications of private statements.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Responses
Hana fis respond: (a) The Lawgiver's authority is absolute, unlike a private person's; (b) The ruling is established by causation, not by a separate command; (c) The cause in the text is transitive by default unless context indicates otherwise; (d) Al-Nazzam's distinction between uttered and omitted causes.
Note the difference between a divine command and a human statement.
5
Understand the Practical Consequence (Thamarah al-Khilaf)
How does this dispute affect actual rulings? Hanafis can extend prohibitions to all intoxicants directly from the text, while opponents require a separate qiyas process. This affects the evidentiary weight and juristic methodology.
The dispute is methodological but has real fqih implications.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة : النص على العلة يكفي في إيجاب تعدية (الحكم في محال تحققها (ولو عدم التعبد بالقياس مطلقاً عند الحنفية و الإمام أحمد وأبي إسحق الشيرازي) الشافعي (وهو المختار، وعليه النظام، لكنه قال إنه منصوص) باستعمال الكلام فيه عرفاً أو لغة (وعند أبي عبدالله البصري المعتزلي يجب التعدية (في التحريم فقط خلافاً للجمهور) من أهل المذاهب لنا أولاً : إن ذكر العلة مع الحكم يفيد تعميمه في محال وجودها، لأنه المتبادر إلى الفهم) من هذا النحو من القرآن (كقول الطبيب لا تأكله لبرودته يفهم منه كل واحد نهيه عن البارد من غیر نظر وفكر، ولا يحتاج في الفهم إلى المعرفة بشرع القياس (و) لنا (ثانياً: لو لم يعم الحكم بل يخص في المنصوص لزم التحكم لأن الظاهر من التعليل (استقلالها) فتخلف الحكم مع وجود العلة المستقلة في بعض المحال دون بعض تحكم صريح، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أن غاية ما لزم من هذا البيان ثبوت الحكم في موارد العلة لا ثبوته مع قطع النظر عن شرع القياس فإنه لو تم لزم عمومه في المنصوصة والمستنبطة جميعاً فافهم. (و) لنا (ثالثاً : حرمت الخمر لأنها مسكرة، في معنى علة الحرمة حقيقة الإسكار عرفاً، فإذا فهم المناظر عرفاً لزم تعميم الحكم أيضاً عرفا (وأما القول بأن حرمة الخمر معلل بالإسكار المنسوب إليه (لا) بالإسكار (مطلقاً، ففي غاية الضعف، لأن الكلام في العلة المتعدية يعني أن الكلام فيما لا تدل القرينة فيه على الاختصاص بل يكون الظاهر فيه التعدية (كقول الطبيب) فإذا فرض الاختصاص خرج عن محل النزاع المنكرون) قالوا أوّلاً: لو ثبت إيجاب التعدية فعن دليل، ولا دليل على الوجوب، وهو الأمر أو الإخبار به ولم يوجد شيء منهما (قلنا) لا نسلم أنه لا دليل بل ثبوت الحكم عن الشارع من (الدلائل وههنا قد ثبت بالتعليل ولا نسلم أن الدليل منحصر في صيغة الأمر أو الإخبار به (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : لو صح وجوب التعدية من دون توقف على شرع القياس (لزم عتق كل أسود عند قوله : أعتقت غانماً لسواده لعموم العلة (قلنا : لا يلزم من حجية إيجاب الشارع على غيره من العبيد (حجية إيجاب أحد على نفسه) يعني : سلمنا أن مفاده عتق كل أسود، لكن لا يلزم لزومه، بخلاف حكم الله تعالى فإنه وال وجبار على الإطلاق (اللهم إلا أن يكون العموم بالصيغة) بأن تكون الصيغة دالة عليه حقيقة أو مجازاً، فإن الشارع إنما أعطاها ولاية الاعتاق وجميع التصرفات الإنشائية بتلفظ الصيغة الدالة عليه (وهو ممنوع) فلا يلزم العتق في غير غانم من السودان لعدم موجبه، وهو اللفظ الدال عليه مطابقة حقيقة أو مجازاً على أن للنظام أن يفرق بين المنطوق والمحذوف) فيقول : الموجب للعتق المنطوق دون المحذوف، وههنا اللفظ وإن عم جميع السودان لكنه محذوف وفيه تأمل، قال (البصري) العلة في التحريم تدل على أن الضرر منها فأينما وجدت وجد الضرر، دفع كل ضرر (واجب) فيعم التحريم جميع محالها بخلاف فعل كل خير فإنه ليس واجباً، والعلة المقارنة للأمر إنما توجب الخيرية فيكون كل محالها خيراً ولا يلزم الوجوب منه (قلنا: إيجاب كل شيء حرمة ضده أي يوجبه (فتركه) أي ترك الواجب (كالنهي) يكون مشتملاً على ضرر يجب دفعه، فوجب العموم (تدبر) فإنه دقيق إلا أن يفرق بما بالذات وما بالعرض، فالأولى أن يقرر منعاً بأنا لا نسلم أن كل فعل خير ليس بواجب، بل الأمر كالنهي في دفع الضرر وطلب الخير فافهم
Issue: The text on the cause suffices to necessitate the extension of the ruling to the places where it is realized, even if there is no commitment to qiyas at all, according to the Hanafis, Imam Ahmad, and Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi al-Shafi'i. And it is the chosen view, and al-Nazzam holds it, but he said it is textual (mansus) by usage of speech customarily or linguistically. According to Abu Abdullah al-Basri al-Mu'tazili, extension is obligatory only in prohibition, contrary to the majority of school scholars. For us, first: Mentioning the cause with the ruling indicates its generalization to the places of its existence, because it is what is immediately understood from this kind of Quranic expression, like the doctor's word: 'Do not eat it because of its coldness'; everyone understands his prohibition of cold things without reflection or thought, and does not need knowledge of the legislation of qiyas to understand. Second: If the ruling were not general but specific to the textually mentioned case, it would be arbitrary, because the apparent meaning of causation is that it is independent. So the absence of the ruling with the presence of the independent cause in some cases but not others is pure arbitrariness. And you do not miss that the utmost of this statement establishes the ruling in the cases of the cause, not its establishment regardless of the legislation of qiyas. For if it were complete, it would necessitate its generality in both textually indicated and derived causes, so understand. Third: Wine is prohibited because it is intoxicating, and the meaning of the cause of prohibition is intoxication in custom. So if the discussant understands it customarily, generalization of the ruling also becomes customary. As for the statement that the prohibition of wine is based on intoxication attributed to it, not on intoxication absolutely, it is extremely weak, because the discussion is about the transitive cause, meaning speech where no context indicates specification, but the apparent meaning is transitivity, like the doctor's word. So if specification is assumed, it leaves the subject of dispute. The deniers said: First: If the obligation of extension were established, it would be by a proof, and there is no proof for obligation, which is a command or an informing, and neither exists. We say: We do not concede that there is no proof; rather, the establishment of a ruling from the Lawgiver is from the proofs, and here it is established by causation, and we do not concede that the proof is limited to the imperative form or informing. They said second: If the obligation of extension without depending on the legislation of qiyas were correct, then every black slave would be freed when one says 'I freed Ghanim because of his blackness' due to the generality of the cause. We say: The authority of the Lawgiver's obligation on others does not necessitate the authority of one's own obligation on himself. That is, we concede that its implication is freeing every black, but its bindingness does not follow, contrary to Allah's ruling, for He is absolute in authority. Unless the generality is by verbal form, meaning the form indicates it literally or figuratively, for the Lawgiver has given the authority of freeing and all performative actions by uttering the form that indicates it, which is denied. So freeing does not follow for other than Ghanim from the blacks due to the absence of its cause, which is the word indicating it directly, literally or figuratively. Moreover, al-Nazzam can distinguish between the uttered and the omitted, saying: The obligator of freeing is the uttered, not the omitted, and here the word, although general for all blacks, is omitted, and there is consideration. Al-Basri said: The cause in prohibition indicates that harm comes from it; wherever it exists, harm exists. Repelling every harm is obligatory, so prohibition generalizes to all its places, unlike every good act, for it is not obligatory. The cause accompanying a command only necessitates goodness, so every place becomes good, but obligation does not follow. We say: Obliging every thing is the prohibition of its opposite, i.e., its abandonment. So leaving the obligatory is like prohibition, containing harm that must be repelled, so generality is needed. Consider, for it is subtle, unless one distinguishes between what is essential and what is accidental. It is better to establish a refusal: we do not concede that every good act is not obligatory; rather, the command is like the prohibition in repelling harm and seeking good. So understand.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage presents a detailed usul dispute about whether an explicit mention of the 'illa (cause) in a legal text obligates extending the same ruling to all cases where that 'illa is found, even without resorting to qiyas. The Hanafis, along with Imam Ahmad and Abu Ishaq al-Shirazi, hold that it does, and this is the chosen view. The Mu'tazili al-Basri restricts it to prohibitions only. The Hanafi proofs: (1) Linguistic common understanding—when a doctor says 'do not eat it because of its coldness,' everyone understands the prohibition of all cold things. (2) If the ruling were specific, it would be arbitrary since the cause appears independent. (3) The prohibition of wine due to intoxication implies all intoxicants are prohibited customarily. The opponents raise objections: There is no explicit command or report obligating extension, and it would lead to absurdities like freeing all black slaves if someone says 'I freed Ghanim for his blackness.' The Hanafi response: The Lawgiver's obligation is authoritative, not a private person's; the ruling extends by virtue of the textual indication, not by personal whim. Also, al-Nazzam distinguishes between uttered and omitted causes. Al-Basri's distinction between prohibition (harm repulsion) and command (good) is answered by noting that leaving a duty causes harm, so the same logic applies.

Key Terms
العلة المتعدية (al-'illa al-muta'addiya): The transitive cause: a cause that is not confined to the specific case but extends to all similar cases.
المنصوص (al-mansus): The text that explicitly mentions the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the third proof for the Hanafi position regarding the obligation of extension when a cause is explicitly mentioned?
A) The doctor analogy
B) The wine analogy (wine is prohibited because it is intoxicating)
C) The argument from arbitrariness
D) The authority of the Lawgiver

Key Takeaway
An explicit cause in a legal text suffices to extend the ruling to all similar instances without requiring qiyas.

Qiyas is Not Applied in Hudud Penalties
Hanafi position and critique on qiyas in hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi argument that qiyas does not apply in hudud and analyse the critique regarding the scope of shubha.

Core Idea
Qiyas cannot establish hudud because any doubt repels the fixed penalty.

This passage presents the Hanafi position that analogy (qiyas) cannot be used to extend hudud penalties, a key point of ikhtilaf with other schools. The Hanafis rely on the hadith 'Avert hudud by doubts' and argue that qiyas, being speculative, introduces doubt. However, the author responds that the doubt in question is factual uncertainty, not methodological speculation—a critique that sharpens our understanding of how legal proofs interact in the hudud domain.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its initial proof
Identify the Hanafi claim that qiyas is not applied in hudud and the first argument: hudud involve rationally incomprehensible estimates (e.g., 100 lashes).
This argument is presented as insufficient by the author.
2
Identify the opposing school's objection
The opponent (other schools) responds that if an original case and its cause are known, analogizing the quantity is possible, so the incomprehensibility claim is not decisive.
This objection shows the weakness of the first argument.
3
Follow the Hanafi secondary proof – the hadith
The Hanafis then cite the hadith 'Avert the hudud by doubts' to argue that the doubt inherent in qiyas repels hadd.
This is the stronger proof.
4
Analyse the author's critique
The author critiques that the hadith refers to doubt in the factual occurrence of the crime, not in the legal proof. The commanded precaution is about establishing the fact, not rejecting a well-founded ruling.
The critique narrows the scope of the hadith.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the stronger argument
The practical difference: Hanafis do not extend hudud via qiyas; others may. The author implies the Hanafi argument needs refinement, but the principle of caution in hudud remains valid.
The Hanafi position is still defensible but requires a more precise formulation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: (الحنفية قالوا لا يجري القياس في الحدود خلافاً لمن عداهم (لاشتمالها) أي الحدود على تقديرات لا تعقل بالرأي (كالمائة) والثمانين هذا دعوى من غير دليل، والخصم لا يقنع عليه، بل يقول عدم معقولية التقادير ابتداء مسلم ولا يضر، وأما إذا وجد أصل وعرف علته فمعقولية التقادير رأياً بالتعدية ليست ممتنعة بل واقعة. ثم أشار إلى دليل آخر لهم بقوله : (ولو (عقل) التقدير كما قيل في اليد السارقة فالشبهة الثابتة في القياس (دارئة) للحد، فلا يثبت لقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : «ادرؤوا الحدود بالشبهات» رواه في بعض السنن وهذا أيضاً غير واف، فإنّ الشبهة الدارئة هي الشبهة في تحقق السبب، والحديث محمول عليه والمأمور به هو الاحتيال في ثبوت الحد كيلا يثبت باستقصاء السؤال عن الشهود وعدم طلب المشهود عليه ونحو ذلك لا إسقاط ما هو ثابت من الشرع بشبهة في دليله غير مانعة عن وجوب العمل، كيف ولو كان مطلق الشبهة مانعاً بالدلائل الظنية كالعام المخصوص ونحوه، وأخبار الآحاد فما قال المصنف أن أخبار الآحاد عن الحد لما وجب الحد
Issue: The Hanafis said: Qiyas does not apply in hudud, contrary to those other than them, because hudud contain estimates that are not rationally comprehensible, like one hundred and eighty. This is a claim without proof, and the opponent is not convinced by it. Rather, he says: The incomprehensibility of the estimates initially is conceded and does not harm. But if an original case is found and its cause is known, then the comprehensibility of the estimates by extension is not impossible but actually occurs. Then he indicated another proof for them by his saying: 'And if the estimation were rational as is said about the hand of the thief, then the doubt established in qiyas repels the hadd, so it is not established.' Due to his saying: 'Avert the hudud by doubts' narrated in some Sunan. And this is also insufficient, for the repelling doubt is doubt in the actualization of the cause, and the hadith is interpreted accordingly. What is commanded is precaution in the establishment of the hadd so that it is not established by exhaustive questioning of witnesses and not seeking the accused, etc., not the negation of what is established from the Shari'ah by doubt in its proof that does not prevent obligation. How so? If every doubt were a preventer, then with Zanni proofs like general texts and similar and ahad reports... so what the author said that ahad reports about hadd prevent the hadd when it becomes obligatory.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage discusses the Hanafi position that qiyas (analogy) is not applied in hudud (fixed penalties) unlike other schools. The initial argument is that hudud involve precise numerical estimates (e.g., 100 lashes for fornication, 80 for slander) that are not rationally derivable. The opponent counters that if an original ruling and its cause are known, then analogizing the quantity is possible. Then a stronger Hanafi argument is presented: The hadith 'Avert the hudud by doubts' indicates that doubts repel hadd penalties, and since qiyas involves an element of doubt (being non-definitive), it cannot establish a hadd. However, the author criticizes this, saying the hadith is about doubt in the factual occurrence, not in the legal proof. The doubt referred to is in the actualization of the cause (e.g., uncertainty about whether the act occurred), not in the validity of the analogy. The hadith commands caution in establishing the penalty, not to reject a well-founded ruling due to speculative proof. The final lines suggest that if every doubt prevented hadd, then rulings from Zanni proofs (like general texts and ahadith) would be impossible, which is unacceptable. The text ends abruptly, but the Hanafi position remains that qiyas is not valid in hudud due to the special nature of these penalties and the sahih principle of repelling them with doubt.

Key Terms
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed punishments prescribed by Shari'ah for major crimes (e.g., theft, fornication, slander).
الشبهة (al-shubha): Doubt that prevents the application of a hadd penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary Hanafi evidence for not applying qiyas in hudud?
A) The Quranic verse on hudud is specific.
B) The hadith 'Avert the hudud by doubts'.
C) Ijma' of the Companions.
D) The rationally incomprehensible nature of hudud estimates.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi position that qiyas does not apply in hudud is based on the hadith 'Avert hudud by doubts', but the scope of 'doubt' is debated—whether it covers methodological doubt (Hanafi view) or only factual doubt (author's critique).

Does a Cause Necessitate Extension? The Hanafi Argument
Debating whether a cause necessitates generalization to all instances

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the dispute over whether a cause ('illah) implies extension and apply the Hanafi argument that the Lawgiver's causation itself is evidence.

Core Idea
The Lawgiver's act of establishing a ruling via a cause is itself evidence of extension, not requiring an explicit command.

This passage addresses a foundational usul debate: when the Lawgiver links a ruling to a cause, does that cause necessarily extend to all instances where the cause is found? The deniers argue that without an explicit command or report, extension is not obligatory. The Hanafi response reframes the nature of evidence itself, asserting that the very act of causation by the Lawgiver is sufficient proof of generality. Understanding this argument is key to grasping the Hanafi methodology of qiyas and textual interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
The passage asks: does a cause ('illah) imply extension (ta'addiyah) to all its instances? The Hanafi school says yes, causation itself suffices; the deniers say no without explicit command or report.
2
Analyze the deniers' first objection
Deniers argue that obligation of extension requires a separate command (amr) or report (khabar), and neither exists. They claim evidence is confined to these forms.
This objection reflects a literalist approach to evidence.
3
Examine the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response: evidence is not confined to command or report; the very establishment of a ruling by the Lawgiver through causation (ta'lil) is itself evidence (dalil). The Lawgiver's act of linking a ruling to a cause indicates that wherever the cause exists, the ruling applies.
This is a key usul principle: the Lawgiver's ta'lil is evidence.
4
Evaluate the second objection and response
Deniers give an example: if one says 'I freed Ghanim because of his blackness', would that free all black slaves? Hanafi reply: no, because the Lawgiver's ruling is different from a human's declaration. Only the Lawgiver's rulings are universally binding. Also, the generality must be expressed by the wording, not omitted.
Distinction between divine and human authority is crucial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالإسكار (مطلقاً، ففي غاية الضعف، لأن الكلام في العلة المتعدية يعني أن الكلام فيما لا تدل القرينة فيه على الاختصاص بل يكون الظاهر فيه التعدية (كقول الطبيب) فإذا فرض الاختصاص خرج عن محل النزاع المنكرون) قالوا أوّلاً: لو ثبت إيجاب التعدية فعن دليل، ولا دليل على الوجوب، وهو الأمر أو الإخبار به ولم يوجد شيء منهما (قلنا) لا نسلم أنه لا دليل بل ثبوت الحكم عن الشارع من (الدلائل وههنا قد ثبت بالتعليل ولا نسلم أن الدليل منحصر في صيغة الأمر أو الإخبار به (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : لو صح وجوب التعدية من دون توقف على شرع القياس (لزم عتق كل أسود عند قوله : أعتقت غانماً لسواده لعموم العلة (قلنا : لا يلزم من حجية إيجاب الشارع على غيره من العبيد (حجية إيجاب أحد على نفسه) يعني : سلمنا أن مفاده عتق كل أسود، لكن لا يلزم لزومه، بخلاف حكم الله تعالى فإنه وال وجبار على الإطلاق (اللهم إلا أن يكون العموم بالصيغة) بأن تكون الصيغة دالة عليه حقيقة أو مجازاً، فإن الشارع إنما أعطاها ولاية الاعتاق وجميع التصرفات الإنشائية بتلفظ الصيغة الدالة عليه (وهو ممنوع) فلا يلزم العتق في غير غانم من السودان لعدم ،موجبه ، وهو اللفظ الدال عليه مطابقة حقيقة أو مجازاً على أن للنظام أن يفرق بين المنطوق والمحذوف) فيقول : الموجب للعتق المنطوق دون المحذوف، وههنا اللفظ وإن عم جميع السودان لكنه محذوف وفيه تأمل، قال (البصري) العلة في التحريم تدل على أن الضرر منها فأينما وجدت وجد الضرر، دفع كل ضرر (واجب) فيعم التحريم جميع محالها بخلاف فعل كل خير فإنه ليس واجباً، والعلة المقارنة للأمر إنما توجب الخيرية فيكون كل محالها خيراً ولا يلزم الوجوب منه (قلنا: إيجاب كل شيء حرمة ضده أي يوجبه (فتركه) أي ترك الواجب (كالنهي) يكون مشتملاً على ضرر يجب دفعه، فوجب العموم (تدبر) فإنه دقيق إلا أن يفرق بما بالذات وما بالعرض، فالأولى أن يقرر منعاً بأنا لا نسلم أن كل فعل خير ليس بواجب، بل الأمر كالنهي في دفع الضرر وطلب الخير فافهم .
Regarding intoxication (absolutely, it is extremely weak, because the discussion concerns the transmissible cause, meaning the discussion is about that which no contextual clue indicates specificity, but rather its apparent meaning is transmissibility (like the doctor's statement). So if specificity is assumed, it exits the domain of dispute). The deniers said: First, if the obligation of transmissibility were established, it would be by evidence, and there is no evidence for obligation, and it is either a command or a report thereof, and neither exists. (We said) We do not accept that there is no evidence; rather, the establishment of a ruling from the Lawgiver is from evidences, and here it has been established by causation, and we do not accept that evidence is confined to the form of a command or a report thereof. (And) They said: Second, if the obligation of transmissibility were valid without depending on the legislation of analogy, then it would necessitate freeing every black slave when one says 'I freed Ghanim because of his blackness' due to the generality of the cause. (We said) The authority of the Lawgiver's obligation on others (i.e., slaves) does not entail the authority of one's own obligation on oneself. Meaning: We accept that its implication is freeing every black slave, but it does not necessitate its occurrence, unlike God's ruling, for He is authoritative and compelling absolutely. (Unless the generality is by the wording) i.e., if the wording indicates it literally or metaphorically, for the Lawgiver has given the authority of manumission and all commissive dispositions by pronouncing the wording that indicates it (and that is denied). So freeing other than Ghanim from black slaves does not follow due to the lack of its cause, which is the wording indicating it literally or metaphorically. Moreover, al-Nazzam can differentiate between the uttered and the omitted, saying: The cause for freeing is the uttered statement, not the omitted one, and here the wording, although general to all black slaves, is omitted, and there is reflection. Al-Basri said: The cause in prohibition indicates that harm arises from it; wherever it exists, harm exists, and repelling every harm is obligatory, so prohibition extends to all its loci, unlike every good deed, for it is not obligatory, and the cause accompanying a command only necessitates goodness, so every locus is good, but obligation does not follow from it. (We said: Obligation of everything is the prohibition of its opposite, i.e., it obligates it, so its abandonment (i.e., abandoning the obligatory) is like prohibition, involving harm that must be repelled, so generality is obligatory. (Reflect) for it is subtle, except that one may distinguish between what is essential and what is accidental. The better approach is to deny by saying we do not accept that every good deed is not obligatory; rather, a command is like a prohibition in repelling harm and seeking good, so understand.)
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage is a debate about whether a cause ('illah) that is associated with a ruling necessarily implies extension (ta'addiyah) to all cases where that cause exists. The author presents the objections of the deniers (al-munkirun) who argue that without explicit command or report, extension is not obligatory. The Hanafi response is that the very establishment of the ruling via the Lawgiver's causation is evidence. The second objection uses the example of freeing a slave due to blackness: if extension were automatic, saying 'I freed Ghanim because of his blackness' would free all black slaves. The Hanafi reply distinguishes between the Lawgiver's authority and human authority—only the Lawgiver's ruling is necessarily general. Al-Basri's argument about harm vs. good is addressed by noting that obligation involves prohibition of opposites, generating harm. The passage ends by noting a subtle distinction between essential and accidental, and reaffirming that commands, like prohibitions, involve repelling harm and seeking good.

Key Terms
العلة المتعدية (al-ʿillah al-mutaʿaddiyah): A cause whose effect extends to all cases where that cause is found, as opposed to a specific cause
التعدية (al-taʿaddiyah): The extension of a ruling from a specific instance to all instances bearing the same cause
العموم بالصيغة (al-ʿumūm bi al-ṣīghah): Generality achieved through the wording itself, either literally or metaphorically

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi argument in the passage, what is the main evidence that a cause implies extension?
A) The existence of an explicit command
B) The existence of a report
C) The establishment of the ruling by the Lawgiver through causation
D) The generality of the wording

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the Lawgiver's establishment of a ruling via a cause is sufficient evidence for that ruling's extension to all instances of the cause, without requiring an explicit command or report.

Qiyas in Hudud and Kaffarat: The Hanafi Position
Arguing that analogical reasoning is invalid in penalties and expiations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that qiyas does not apply to hudud and kaffarat, identify the key textual evidence, and evaluate the opposing school's argument.

Core Idea
Hudud and kaffarat are ruled by fixed divine quantities; analogical reasoning introduces doubt and thus cannot establish them.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut tackles a foundational usul dispute: can qiyas be used to extend hudud and kaffarat? The Hanafi school says no, basing itself on the nature of these rulings and a crucial hadith. We'll unpack the proof and the counterarguments, focusing on the interpretive moves that define the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi ruling
State clearly that the Hanafis hold qiyas invalid in hudud and kaffarat. Note the reason: fixed quantities ('taqdirat') not comprehensible by reason.
This is the core claim to be defended.
2
Examine the primary dalil
Analyze the hadith 'idra'u al-hudud bi al-shubuhat.' How do the Hanafis interpret 'shubuhat'? They narrow it to doubt in the actual occurrence of the cause, not doubt in the evidentiary basis.
This narrow interpretation is key to the argument.
3
Analyze the opposing school's proof
The opponent cites the general authority of qiyas and the companion example of 'Ali's analogy for the wine penalty. Understand each proof.
The opponent's strongest evidence is the historical practice.
4
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: 1) General proofs for qiyas are restricted by a preventer (al-taqdir). 2) 'Ali's analogy was either based on consensus or on prophetic indications, not pure qiyas. 3) The hadith on doubts is not overridden; qiyas itself introduces a doubt that prevents hudud.
The Hanafi response relies on rational specification (takhsis 'aqli).
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: whether a new intoxicant (like a synthetic drug) can be punished by the hadd for wine via qiyas. Hanafi: no; Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali: yes.
This shows real-world impact of the usul position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

التقادير ابتداء مسلم ولا يضر، وأما إذا وجد أصل وعرف علته فمعقولية التقادير رأياً بالتعدية ليست ممتنعة بل واقعة. ثم أشار إلى دليل آخر لهم بقوله : (ولو (عقل) التقدير كما قيل في اليد السارقة فالشبهة الثابتة في القياس (دارئة) للحد، فلا يثبت لقوله صلى الله عليه وآله وأصحابه وسلم : «ادرؤوا الحدود بالشبهات» رواه في بعض السنن وهذا أيضاً غير واف، فإنّ الشبهة الدارئة هي الشبهة في تحقق السبب، والحديث الشبهة مانعاً بالدلائل الظنية كالعام المخصوص ونحوه، وأخبار الآحاد فما قال المصنف أن أخبار الآحاد عن الحد لما وجب الحد مثل القياس في عدم الإثبات فلا ينقض بها غير نافع مع أنه قد تقدم أن الرواية عن الإمام أبي يوسف ثبوت الحدود بخبر الواحد، وكذا لا ينفع الجواب بأن خبر الواحد ليس في دلالته وإثباته ضعف. وإنما الضعف في السند بخلاف القياس، فإن الضعف في أصل دلالته لأنه لا يعم جميع صور النقض. ولأن الفرق بين الضعفين تحكم فإنّ كليهما يوجبان شبهة عدم الثبوت فافهم المثبتون (قالوا : أولاً : أدلة الحجية) أي حجية القياس (عامة) لجميع الأقيسة في حدود كان أو في غيرها، فيجب القول بحجية جميع الأقيسة (قلنا) لا نسلم أنها عامة (بل مخصصة بعدم المانع ، فإنه) تخصيص (عقلي) كيف وقد مرّ الشروط في الحجية، فالقياس الغير المشتمل على بعضها غير حجة، والقياس في الحدود من هذا القبيل لأن التقدير مانع (و) قالوا :(ثانياً : حد في الخمر زمن الصحابة رضوان الله تعالى عليهم (بقياس) أمير المؤمنين (علي) كرّم الله وجهه ووجوه آله الكرام كما مرّ (قلنا) لم يحد في الخمر بالقياس (بل بالإجماع) المزيل لشبهة القياس (ولا) يلزم منه أي من الجواز بالقياس المزال الشبهة (الجواز) بالقياس (مطلقاً) ولا يذهب عليك ما فيه أولاً أن هذا الكلام إن أورد نقضاً على الدليل الأول لا يتوجه هذا الجواب. فإنه قد عقل بالرأي التقدير وثانياً : إن الإجماع إنما ينعقد بالاستدلال بالقياس. وإذ قد استدل أهل الإجماع به لم يكن مزال الشبهة أصلاً، وإنما زالت شبهته بعد تقرر الإجماع، فعلم بعمل أهل الإجماع أن الشبهة الراسخة في القياس غير مانعة عن العمل به في الحدود على أنه كان الحد عليه باجتماع أدلة سمعية عليه عندنا ولم يكن بالقياس، وفيه استدلال أمير المؤمينن علي رضي الله عنه بحضرة أمير المؤمنين عمر رضي الله عنه ومشهد من الصحابة مع عدم إنكارهم عليه يفيد أن التعبد به في الحدود كان جائزاً عندهم، وهذا لا ينافي الاجتماع أدلة سمعية عليه أيضاً فافهم. ثم أورد عليه أيضاً أن الأدلة السمعية ما دلّت على أن حد الشرب ثمانون وهذا إنما يثبت بالقياس لا غير ويؤيده ما روى الحاكم عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه أن أهل الشرب كانوا يضربون على عهد رسول الله بالأيدي والنعال والعصي حتى توفي فكان أبو بكر يجلد أربعين حتى توفي إلى أن قال : فقال عمر رضي الله عنه : ماذا ترون؟ فقال علي رضي الله عنه : إذا شرب سكر، وإذا سكر هذى وإذا هذى افترى، وعلى المفتري ثمانون. فإذن علم أن تحديد ثمانين بالقياس لا غير. وأجيب أن المقصود أن حده كان أخذ بإشارات رسول الله ، وكان أمره في الزيادة والنقصان موقوفاً على فساد الزمان وصلاحه، ولذا زادوا ثم أجمعوا على ثمانين منعاً للزيادة عليه عند ظهور فساد شديد، فمراتب الحدود كانت مأخوذة من صاحب الشرع والرأي لتعيين كل عدد بحسب الزمان، ويؤيده ما روى البخاري عن السائب بن يزيد قال : كنا نؤتي بالشارب على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و وامراة أبي بكر وصدراً من خلافة عمر، فنقوم إليه بأيدينا ونعالنا وأرديتنا حتى كان آخر إمرة عمر فجلد أربعين، حتى إذا عتوا وفسقوا جلد ثمانين . هكذا قالوا ( ثم) الكفارات كالحدود) في الخلاف المذكور، فالحنفية قالوا : لا يجري القياس فيها، لأنّ الكفارة ساترة للذنوب، ولا يهتدي إليه العقل، ولأنها مندرئة بالشبهات وفي القياس شبهة وغيرهم قالوا نعم يجري فيها لعموم الأدلة .
Issue: The Hanafis said: Qiyas does not apply to hudud, contrary to those other than them (because hudud involve quantities not comprehensible by reason, like one hundred and eighty. This is a claim without proof, and the opponent is not convinced; rather, he says that the incomprehensibility of quantities initially is conceded but not harmful. But if an original is found and its cause known, then the comprehensibility of quantities by reason through extension is not impossible but occurring. Then he pointed to another evidence for them by saying: (If the quantification is understood as is said in the case of the thief's hand, then the doubt established in qiyas wards off the hadd, so it is not established due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Ward off hudud by doubts' reported in some Sunan. This is also insufficient, for the warding-off doubt is the doubt in the realization of the cause, and the hadith is applied to that. What is commanded is precaution in establishing the hadd so that it is not established by exhaustive questioning of witnesses and not seeking the accused, etc., not dropping what is established from the Shari'ah by a doubt in its evidence that does not prevent obligation. How so? If absolute doubt were preventive, then by probabilistic evidences like a general text that has been specified and similar, and solitary reports. So what the author said that solitary reports are like qiyas in not establishing is not useful, given that it has preceded that the narration from Imam Abu Yusuf is that hudud are established by solitary report. Similarly, the answer that a solitary report has no weakness in its indication and establishment is not useful; rather, the weakness is in the chain, unlike qiyas, for the weakness is in its very indication because it does not cover all forms of criticism. And because the distinction between the two weaknesses is arbitrary, for both cause a doubt of non-establishment, so understand. The affirmers said: First, the evidences for authority (i.e., of qiyas) are general for all analogies, whether in hudud or other, so it is obligatory to say that all analogies are authoritative. (We said) We do not accept that they are general; rather, they are specified by the absence of a preventer, for it is a rational specification. How so? The conditions for authority have passed; analogy lacking some of them is not authoritative, and analogy in hudud is of this type because quantification is a preventer. (And) They said: Second, wine was punished in the time of the Companions by the analogy of the Commander of the Faithful 'Ali, may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family, as has passed. (We said) He did not punish wine by analogy but by consensus that removes the doubt of analogy. The permissibility by analogy whose doubt is removed does not entail permissibility absolutely. Do not overlook what is in it: first, if this speech is presented as an objection to the first evidence, this answer is not relevant, for the quantification was understood by reason. Second, consensus is only established by inference through analogy. Since the people of consensus inferred by it, it did not remove the doubt originally; rather, its doubt was removed after the establishment of consensus. So it is known by the action of the people of consensus that the deep-seated doubt in analogy is not preventative of acting by it in hudud, while the hadd upon him was by a collection of scriptural evidences according to us and not by analogy. In it is the inference of Amir al-Mu'minin 'Ali in the presence of Amir al-Mu'minin 'Umar and the sight of the Companions with their lack of objection to him, which indicates that acting by it in hudud was permissible in their view. This does not contradict the collection of scriptural evidences upon it as well, so understand. Then it was also objected that scriptural evidences did not indicate that the hadd for drinking is eighty; that is only established by qiyas alone. Supported by what al-Hakim narrated from Ibn 'Abbas that the people of drinking were beaten in the time of the Messenger of Allah with hands, sandals, and sticks until he died. Then Abu Bakr used to lash forty until he died. Until he said: 'Umar said: What do you think? 'Ali said: If he drinks, he becomes intoxicated; if he becomes intoxicated, he raves; if he raves, he slanders, and the slanderer has eighty. Thus it is known that the determination of eighty is by qiyas alone. The answer is that the point is that its hadd was taken from the indications of the Messenger of Allah, and his command regarding increase and decrease was dependent on the corruption or righteousness of the time. Hence they increased and then agreed on eighty to prevent increase upon it when severe corruption appeared. The levels of hudud were taken from the Lawgiver and opinion to determine each number according to the time. Supported by what al-Bukhari narrated from al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid: We used to bring the drinker in the time of the Messenger of Allah, and the rule of Abu Bakr and early part of 'Umar's caliphate, and we would stand up to him with our hands, sandals, and garments. Until the end of 'Umar's rule, he lashed forty. Then when they became rebellious and sinful, he lashed eighty. Thus they said. (Then) Expations (kaffarat) are like hudud in the mentioned dispute. The Hanafis said: Qiyas does not apply to them because expiation covers sins, and reason does not guide to it, and because they are warded off by doubts, and in qiyas there is doubt. Others said: Yes, it applies to them due to the generality of the evidences.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position that qiyas does not apply to hudud (fixed penalties) or kaffarat (expiation's). The reason given is that hudud involve fixed quantities (like 100 lashes for adultery, 80 for slander) that are not comprehensible by rational analogy. The opponents argue that once an original and its cause are known, such quantities can be extended. The Hanafi response invokes the hadith 'Ward off hudud by doubts,' but interprets it narrowly: the doubt must be in the actual occurrence of the cause, not in the evidentiary basis of the ruling. The passage then refutes the opponents' claim that the Companions used qiyas for the wine punishment. 'Ali's analogy is explained away as either based on consensus (which removes doubt) or on indications from the Prophet that allowed adjustment according to time. Historical reports show that the number of lashes varied, indicating that the specific number was not fixed by pure qiyas but by collective agreement based on prophetic guidance. Finally, the same reasoning extends to kaffarat: they are not subject to qiyas due to their nature of covering sins and being subject to shubuhat.

Key Terms
الحدود (al-ḥudūd): Fixed corporal punishments prescribed by the Shari'ah for certain crimes, such as flogging for adultery and slander
الكفارات (al-kaffārāt): Expiation's, acts of worship prescribed to expiate certain sins or omissions, such as freeing a slave or fasting
القياس (al-qiyās): Analogical reasoning to derive a legal ruling for a new case based on an original case with a shared cause
الشبهة (al-shubhah): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of a hadd penalty

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why do Hanafis hold that qiyas does not apply to hudud?
A) Because hudud are based on consensus alone
B) Because hudud involve fixed quantities not comprehensible by reason and are subject to doubt
C) Because the Companions never used qiyas for hudud
D) Because hudud are only established by solitary reports

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school excludes hudud and kaffarat from qiyas because they involve fixed quantities and are warded off by doubts; qiyas itself introduces a doubt that would prevent their application.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Restricting Qiyas in Hudud and Kaffarat: The Hanafi Position
Refutation of objections to qiyas in hudud and kaffarat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi argument against qiyas in hudud and kaffarat and evaluate the opposing proof from Ali's qiyas for wine penalty.

Core Idea
Qiyas is invalid in hudud and kaffarat because general proofs are restricted by a preventer (mani').

This passage presents a classic usul dispute: can analogical reasoning (qiyas) be used to establish fixed punishments (hudud) and expiations (kaffarat)? The Hanafi school argues it cannot, due to a rational specification that considers the nature of these rulings. The opposing view cites the general authority of qiyas and the famous example of Ali's qiyas for the hadd of wine. The Hanafi response refutes these arguments, emphasizing that hudud are based on textual certainty and that any doubt (shubha) in the evidence averts punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
What is the dispute about? Is qiyas valid in hudud and kaffarat? Note the two sides: those who affirm general authority and those who restrict it.
2
Examine the opponent's first argument
The opponent argues that the proofs for qiyas are general ('amma) and apply to all cases, including hudud. Identify the basis: 'Adillat al-hujjiyya 'amma'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafis respond that the general proofs are not absolute but are rationally specified by the absence of a preventer (mani'). Qiyas in hudud lacks a condition for validity because the estimation of punishment is a preventer.
Key phrase: 'بل مخصصة بعدم المانع، فإنه تخصيص عقلي'.
4
Evaluate the second argument: Ali's qiyas
The opponent cites Ali's analogy for 80 lashes for wine. The Hanafi response: it was based on consensus (ijma') and prophetic indications, not pure qiyas. Also, the number was adjusted according to societal conditions.
Reference the hadith from al-Hakim and al-Bukhari.
5
Understand the extension to kaffarat
The same reasoning applies to expiations: qiyas is invalid because kaffarat are hidden from intellect and repel doubts. Others permit it due to general proofs.
Final paragraph: 'ثم الكفارات كالحدود'.

حجية القياس (عامة) لجميع الأقيسة في حدود كان أو في غيرها، فيجب القول بحجية جميع الأقيسة (قلنا) لا نسلم أنها عامة (بل مخصصة بعدم المانع ، فإنه) تخصيص (عقلي) كيف وقد مرّ الشروط في الحجية، فالقياس الغير أورد نقضاً على الدليل الأول لا يتوجه هذا الجواب. فإنه قد عقل بالرأي التقدير وثانياً : إن الإجماع إنما ينعقد بالاستدلال بالقياس. وإذ قد استدل أهل الإجماع به لم يكن مزال الشبهة أصلاً، وإنما زالت شبهته
