رضي الله عنه بحضرة أمير المؤمنين عمر رضي الله عنه ومشهد من الصحابة مع عدم إنكارهم عليه يفيد أن التعبد به في الحدود كان جائزاً عندهم، وهذا لا ينافي الاجتماع أدلة سمعية عليه أيضاً فافهم. ثم أورد عليه أيضاً أن الأدلة السمعية ما دلّت على أن حد الشرب ثمانون وهذا إنما يثبت بالقياس لا غير ويؤيده ما روى الحاكم عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنه أن أهل الشرب كانوا يضربون على عهد رسول الله بالأيدي والنعال والعصي حتى توفي فكان أبو بكر يجلد أربعين حتى توفي إلى أن قال : فقال عمر رضي الله عنه : ماذا ترون؟ فقال علي رضي الله عنه : إذا شرب سكر، وإذا سكر هذى وإذا هذى افترى، وعلى المفتري ثمانون. فإذن علم أن تحديد ثمانين بالقياس لا غير. وأجيب أن المقصود أن حده كان أخذ بإشارات رسول الله ، وكان أمره في الزيادة والنقصان موقوفاً على فساد الزمان وصلاحه، ولذا زادوا ثم أجمعوا على ثمانين منعاً للزيادة عليه عند ظهور فساد شديد، فمراتب الحدود كانت مأخوذة من صاحب الشرع والرأي لتعيين كل عدد بحسب الزمان، ويؤيده ما روى البخاري عن السائب بن يزيد قال : كنا نؤتي بالشارب على عهد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم و امراة أبي بكر وصدراً من خلافة عمر، فنقوم إليه بأيدينا ونعالنا وأرديتنا حتى كان آخر إمرة عمر فجلد أربعين، حتى إذا عتوا وفسقوا جلد ثمانين . هكذا قالوا ( ثم) الكفارات كالحدود) في الخلاف المذكور، فالحنفية قالوا : لا يجري القياس فيها، لأنّ الكفارة ساترة للذنوب، ولا يهتدي إليه العقل، ولأنها مندرئة بالشبهات وفي القياس شبهة وغيرهم قالوا نعم يجري فيها لعموم الأدلة .
The fourth principle: Qiyas is like qiyas in not being probative, so refuting it is not beneficial. Moreover, it has been mentioned that the narration from Imam Abu Yusuf establishes hudud by khabar al-wahid, nor does the answer that khabar al-wahid has no weakness in its indication and probity; rather the weakness is in the chain, unlike qiyas, for the weakness is in the basis of its indication because it does not cover all forms of refutation. And the difference between the two weaknesses is arbitrary, for both cause doubt of non-establishment. So understand, O affirmers. (They said: first: general proofs of authority) i.e., the authority of qiyas (are general) for all analogies whether in hudud or others, so it is necessary to affirm the authority of all analogies. (We said) we do not concede that they are general (rather they are specific by the absence of a preventer, for it is) a (rational) specification. How can it be otherwise when the conditions for authority have been mentioned? So qiyas lacking some of these conditions is not authoritative, and qiyas in hudud is of this kind because the estimation is a preventer. (And) they said: (secondly: a hadd was established for wine in the time of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them, (by analogy) of the Commander of the Faithful (Ali), may Allah honor his face and the faces of his noble family, as mentioned. (We said) he did not establish the hadd for wine by qiyas (but by consensus) which removes the doubt of qiyas. (Nor) does it follow from that—i.e., permissibility by qiyas with doubt removed—(permissibility) by qiyas (absolutely). And do not be unmindful of what is in it: first, this speech if it is brought as a refutation against the first proof, this answer does not apply, for it is understood by opinion (ra'y) and estimation. Second, consensus is only formed by inference through qiyas. When the people of consensus have inferred by it, it does not remove the doubt at all; rather its doubt is removed after the establishment of consensus. So it is known by the action of the people of consensus that the rooted doubt in qiyas does not prevent acting upon it in hudud. Moreover, the hadd was established by a combination of textual evidences in our view and was not by qiyas. Also, the inference of the Commander of the Faithful Ali, may Allah be pleased with him, in the presence of the Commander of the Faithful Umar, may Allah be pleased with him, and the presence of the Companions without their denial indicates that acting by it in hudud was permissible according to them. This does not preclude the combination of textual evidences also. So understand. Then it was also objected that the textual evidences did not indicate that the hadd for drinking is eighty; this is only established by qiyas alone. It is supported by what al-Hakim narrated from Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with him, that the people of drinking were beaten in the time of the Messenger of Allah with hands, sandals, and sticks until he died. Then Abu Bakr flogged forty until he died. Then Umar said: 'What do you think?' Ali said: 'When he drinks, he becomes intoxicated; when he becomes intoxicated, he raves; when he raves, he slanders; and for the slanderer there are eighty.' So it is known that determining eighty is by qiyas alone. And the answer is that the intended meaning is that his hadd was taken from the indications of the Messenger of Allah, and its increase or decrease was dependent on the corruption or rectitude of the time. Hence they increased it and then agreed on eighty to prevent increase upon it when severe corruption appeared. Thus the levels of hudud were taken from the Lawgiver, and opinion is for determining each number according to the time. It is supported by what al-Bukhari narrated from al-Sa'ib ibn Yazid: 'We used to bring the drinker in the time of the Messenger of Allah and Abu Bakr and the early part of Umar's caliphate, and we would stand up and beat him with our hands, sandals, and cloaks, until the end of Umar's rule he flogged forty, and when they became rebellious and sinful he flogged eighty.' Thus they said. (Then) expiations are like hudud in the mentioned dispute. The Hanafis said: qiyas does not apply in them because the expiation covers sins and the intellect does not guide to it, and because it is repelled by doubts and qiyas contains doubt. Others said: yes, it applies in them due to generality of proofs.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute on the application of qiyas (analogical reasoning) in hudud (fixed punishments) and kaffarat (expiation). The text presents a Hanafi defense against objections from those who affirm qiyas broadly. The objectors argue that the general proofs for qiyas apply to all categories, including hudud. The Hanafi response is that these proofs are not absolute; they are restricted by the absence of a preventer (mani'), and in hudud there is an inherent preventer (estimation of punishment). The objectors cite the example of Ali's qiyas for the hadd of wine (eighty lashes). The Hanafi counter that the hadd was actually established by consensus (ijma'), not pure qiyas, and that any doubt (shubha) in qiyas is removed by that consensus. Another objection is that textual evidence does not specify eighty, so it must be from qiyas. The Hanafi reply is that the number was taken from prophetic indications, with flexibility based on societal conditions. The passage then extends the same reasoning to kaffarat, where Hanafis reject qiyas because kaffarat are hidden from intellect and repel doubts, while others permit it due to general proofs.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: extending a ruling from an original case to a new case based on a common effective cause (illa).
الحدود (al-hudud): Fixed punishments defined by Shari'ah for specific crimes (e.g., theft, zina, drinking).
مانع (mani'): Preventer: a factor that blocks the application of a general ruling or principle. Here it prevents qiyas from applying in hudud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, why is qiyas not valid in hudud?
A) Because hudud are not mentioned in the Quran or Sunnah
B) Because there is a preventer (mani') that restricts the general proofs for qiyas
C) Because qiyas is always weak in its indication
D) Because the Companions did not use qiyas in hudud

Key Takeaway
The Hanafis restrict qiyas in hudud and kaffarat due to a rational specification based on the presence of a preventer, rejecting the argument that qiyas is universally applicable.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning

Qiyas in Causes, Conditions, and Rulings: A Dispute in Hanafi Usul
Dispute on the validity of qiyas in establishing causes, conditions, and rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions on whether qiyas can establish causes, conditions, and grounds, and explain how the dispute reduces to methodological choices (ta'thir, munasabah, irsal).

Core Idea
Qiyas can extend causes and conditions only if you require effectiveness or accept suitability.

This passage tackles a nuanced dispute: can qiyas be used not just to extend rulings but to establish the very causes, conditions, and grounds that underpin rulings? While all agree that inventing new causes without a textual basis is forbidden, scholars differ on whether we can analogize from an existing cause to a new one. The Hanafi school itself is divided, with Fakhr al-Islam permitting it and a majority (per al-Kashf) prohibiting it. The author resolves this by tying it to one's theory of causation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed-upon starting point
Note the passage's opening: there is no disagreement that causes, conditions, and rulings themselves cannot be established by qiyas without a text. This sets the boundary of the dispute.
The dispute is not about inventing new causes but about extending existing ones via qiyas.
2
State the two positions and their proponents
The permissive view is held by many Hanafis (Fakhr al-Islam) and Shafi'is. The restrictive view is held by other Hanafis (majority per al-Kashf) and Ibn al-Hajib (Maliki).
Know the key figures: Fakhr al-Islam (permitter), Ibn al-Hajib (denier).
3
Trace the proofs of each side
Permitters argue that causality is a ruling like any other, so restricting qiyas is arbitrary, and they cite Companion examples. Deniers argue that the commonality may not be the actual cause, so qiyas should be limited to extending rulings.
The deniers' key point: the manat (relevant factor) might not be the illah itself.
4
Analyze the resolution: verbal dispute and methodological basis
The author suggests the dispute is verbal and ultimately reduces to whether one requires effectiveness (ta'thir) in causation or is satisfied with suitability (munasabah) or free-consideration (irsal). This determines whether qiyas can establish new causes.
This is the crux: the scope of qiyas depends on your theory of causation.
5
Apply to the examples given
Study the examples: Ali's qiyas of drunkenness on slander, and other analogies. Identify which side would accept each example and why.
The examples illustrate the permissive view in action.

Source Text

مسألة: هل يجري القياس في العلل والشروط لا خلاف في أنه لا تثبت العلل وأوصافها كعلية الجنسية في ربا النساء وصفة السوم في نصاب الزكاة ولا الشروط وأوصافها، كاشتراط الشهود في النكاح وذكورتها مثلاً، ولا الأحكام وأوصافها، كجواز البتيراء ووجوب الوتر ابتداء من غير نص مقيس عليه، فإنّ هذا نصب الشرع بالرأي من غير حجة شرعية، بل إنما أمر القياس تعدية حكم أصل إلى مسكوت بجامع، ثم اختلفوا هل تصح هذه التعدية في العلل والشروط والأسباب بأن توجد علة أو سبب أو شرط لحكم لأجل مناط، فيقاس ما يوجد فيه المناط عليها، ويحكم بعليتها وبسببيتها وشرطيتها فكثير من الحنفية) ومنهم الإمام فخر الإسلام والشافعية نعم يجوز (وكثير) قالوا : (لا) يجوز واختاره ابن الحاجب) المالكي. قال «الكشف»: وعليه عامة أصحابنا فيما أظن والذي يدل على أن هذا الحبر الهمام أعني فخر الإسلام على الجواز قوله بعد إبانة أن هذه الأمور لا تثبت بالقياس وإنما أنكرنا هذه الجملة إذا لم يوجد له في الشريعة أصل يصح تعليله، فأما إذا وجد فلا بأس به. المنكرون قالوا: إن استقل الجامع فهو العلة إن كان مضبوطاً وإلا فمظنته وكل من الأصل والفرع من أفراده. وكذا الحال في الشرط، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه يجوز أن لا يكون المناط علة لأصل الحكم وإن كان مضبوطاً، بل إنما هو مناط لعلية العلة وشرطية الشرط، فلا يلزم من وجوده في الفرع إلاّ كونه علة أو شرطاً، لا أن يكون من أفراد العلة فافهم ودليل المجوزين أن العلية والسببية والشرطية أحكام من أحكام الله تعالى كالوجوب والندب وغير ذلك، فتخصيص القياس ببعض الأحكام دون بعض تحكم كيف والأمر بالاعتبار، وكذا عمل الصحابة غير مختص بصورة دون صورة أما تذكر قول أمير المؤمنين علي الأمير المؤمنين عمر كيف قاس سببية الشرب على سببية القذف، وكيف قاسوا : أنت حرام عليّ أنت طالق بائن . ثم لو تدبرت الفقه علمت أن مشايخنا لا يبالون بالقياس في الأسباب والشروط فافهم. ثم بعضهم جعلوا الخلاف لفظياً، بأن المجوز إنما يجوز إثبات سببية شيء لحكم بالقياس على ما هو سبب لذلك الحكم، والمانع إنما يمنع قياس سببية شيء لحكم على سببية آخر لحكم آخر، ولم يوجد لهذا التمحل أثر في كلماتهم وبعضهم قالوا الخلاف إنما هو في المستنبطة دون المنصوصة، قال المصنف (والحق أنه أي هذا المختلف فيه كالمتفق عليه في اشتراط التأثير أو كفاية المناسبة أو تجويز الإرسال فمن شرط التأثير في التعليل لأحكام شرط ههنا أيضاً، ومن اكتفى بما عداه فيها اكتفى ههنا أيضاً لأن الفرق بينهما (تحكم) فإن المسلك مسلك على كل تقدير (إلا أنه لا إلحاق على الآخيرين لاستقلال المسلك فإنه حينئذ لا بد في المقيس من مناسبة يكون بها علة من غير حاجة إلى أمر آخر كالتأثير وغيره فلا يحتاج إلى أصل يلحق به فافهم. (ومثال ذلك) أي القياس في الأسباب ونحوها (قياس) أمير المؤمنين ( علي السكر على القذف بجامع الافتراء، وقياس الردة على السرقة الكبرى للحكمة الضرورية فالأول فيه هتك الدين، والثاني فيه هتك المال وإلى كل منهما حاجة ضرورية (وأما المثقل) أي قياسه على المحدّد للقصاص) بجامع القتل العمد العدوان والأكل) أي قياسه على الوقاع للكفارة) لكونه جناية
Question: Does qiyas apply to causes and conditions? There is no disagreement that causes and their attributes are not established (by qiyas alone), like the causality of kind in riba al-nisa' and the attribute of grazing (sa'ima) in the nisab of zakat, nor conditions and their attributes, like the requirement of witnesses in marriage and their being male, for example, nor rulings and their attributes, like the permissibility of al-batira' and the obligation of witr initially without a text to be analogized upon. For this would be legislating by opinion without a legal proof. Rather the matter of qiyas is to extend the ruling of an original case to an unmentioned case via a commonality. Then they disagreed whether this extension is valid in causes, conditions, and grounds; i.e., when there exists a cause, ground, or condition for a ruling due to a relevant factor (manat), can one analogize on it and rule that it is a cause, ground, or condition? Many Hanafis, including Imam Fakhr al-Islam, and the Shafi'is say yes it is permissible. Many others said no, it is not permissible, and Ibn al-Hajib (the Maliki) chose this. Al-Kashf said: And upon this are most of our companions, I think. And what indicates that this great scholar, I mean Fakhr al-Islam, was for permissibility is his statement after explaining that these things are not established by qiyas: 'We only denied this entirety when there is no origin in the Shari'ah that can be properly attributed; if there is, then there is no problem.' The deniers said: If the commonality is independent, it is the cause if it is well-defined, otherwise it is its locus (mazannah). And both the original and the branch are instances of it. Similarly for the condition. And do not be unaware that it is possible that the relevant factor is not the cause of the original ruling even if it is well-defined; rather it is a factor for the causality of the cause and conditionality of the condition. So its presence in the branch only necessitates it being a cause or a condition, not that it is an instance of the cause. Understand. And the proof of those who permit is that causality, ground-hood, and conditionality are rulings of Allah like obligation and recommendation and so on. So restricting qiyas to some rulings without others is arbitrary. How can that be when there is the command to consider (i'tibar)? Also the practice of the Companions is not restricted to one type without another. Do you not remember the saying of the Commander of the Faithful Ali to the Commander of the Faithful Umar: how he analogized the ground-hood of drinking on the ground-hood of slander? And how they analogized: 'You are forbidden to me, you are divorced with a final divorce'? Then if you reflect on fiqh, you know that our shuyukh do not care about qiyas in grounds and conditions. So understand. Then some made the dispute verbal: the permissibility is about establishing the causality of something for a ruling by qiyas on something that is a cause for that ruling, and the prohibition is about analogizing the causality of one thing for a ruling on the causality of another thing for another ruling. And this fabrication has no trace in their words. Some others said the dispute is only about deduced (mustanbitah) causes, not explicit (mansusah) ones. The author said: The truth is that this disputed matter is like an agreed-upon matter regarding requiring effectiveness (ta'thir) or sufficiency of suitability (munasabah) or allowing free-consideration (irsal). So whoever requires effectiveness in causation for rulings requires it here too, and whoever is satisfied with what is other than it there is satisfied here too, because the difference between them is arbitrary. For the path is a path in every estimation. However, there is no annexation (ilhaq) for the latter two because the path is self-sufficient; then there is no need for an origin to annex to. Understand. An example of this (i.e., qiyas in grounds and the like) is the qiyas of the Commander of the Faithful Ali of drunkenness on slander by the commonality of slander. And the qiyas of apostasy on major theft for the necessary wisdom: the first involves violation of religion, the second violation of wealth, and each of them has a necessary need. As for a heavy object (al-muthqal), i.e., analogizing it on a sharp weapon for retaliation by the commonality of intentional transgressive killing. And eating, i.e., analogizing it on intercourse for expiation because it is a transgression.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute in Hanafi usul: whether qiyas can be used to establish causes (ilal), conditions (shurut), and grounds (asbab) for rulings. The text clarifies an initial point of agreement: that causes, conditions, and rulings themselves cannot be invented by qiyas without a textual basis. The disagreement is about extending an existing cause/condition from one case to another via qiyas. A group of Hanafis (e.g., Fakhr al-Islam) and Shafi'is permit this, arguing that causality, conditionality, etc., are all rulings of Allah, and it would be arbitrary to restrict qiyas to some rulings. They cite examples from the Companions, like Ali's qiyas of drinking to slander. Another group, including Ibn al-Hajib, reject it. The author (of the matn) suggests the dispute may be verbal and traces it back to whether one requires effectiveness (ta'thir) in causation or is satisfied with suitability (munasabah) or free-consideration (irsal). The passage ends with examples of qiyas in grounds: drunkenness on slander, apostasy on theft, heavy object on sharp weapon for retaliation, and eating on intercourse for expiation.

Key Terms
العلة (al-illah): The effective cause (ratio legis) in qiyas that necessitates a ruling.
الشرط (al-shart): A condition that is necessary for a ruling but not its cause (e.g., witnesses in marriage).
المناط (al-manat): The relevant factor or attribute that is considered in qiyas; it may be the cause itself or merely the locus of the cause.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main point of disagreement in this passage?
A) Whether qiyas can create new rulings without any text
B) Whether qiyas can establish causes, conditions, and grounds for rulings
C) Whether the Companions used qiyas at all
D) Whether qiyas is a valid source of law

Key Takeaway
Whether qiyas can establish causes, conditions, and grounds is a legitimate dispute that ultimately hinges on one's theory of causation (ta'thir vs. munasabah vs. irsal).

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
advanced
8 min
The Validity of Qiyas in Causes, Conditions, and Reasons
Dispute on qiyas in illal, shurut, asbab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the positions and proofs in the dispute over whether qiyas can establish illal, shurut, and asbab, and evaluate the Hanafi tarjih.

Core Idea
Qiyas can establish causes, conditions, and reasons because these are rulings like any other, and the Companions practised it.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut tackles a key usul question: can qiyas be used to prove that something is a cause (illah), condition (shart), or reason (sabab) for a ruling? While all agree that inventing a cause purely by opinion is invalid, there is debate over whether qiyas can extend a recognized cause to a new situation. The author presents the views of both sides, leaning toward permissibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Determine what exactly is being disputed: not whether qiyas can create a new cause from nothing, but whether it can establish that something is a cause, condition, or reason by analogy.
This is a subtle point – the disagreement is about extending existing causes.
2
State the two main positions
The permissibility camp (many Hanafis including Fakhr al-Islam, and Shafi'is) allows it; the prohibition camp (some Hanafis and Ibn al-Hajib) forbids it.
Note that the opposing school includes both Hanafis and non-Hanafis.
3
Examine the proofs for permissibility
The permissibility side argues that causehood is a divine ruling like wujub, so qiyas applies. They cite the practice of the Companions, especially Ali and Umar (RA), who performed qiyas on causes (e.g., intoxication vs. slander).
They also invoke the general command to 'consider' (i'tibar) in the Quran.
4
Examine the proofs for prohibition
The prohibition camp argues that the commonality (jami') must be precisely defined and belong to the same category as the original cause; otherwise, it is mere conjecture.
They fear that allowing qiyas in causes could lead to arbitrary legislation.
5
Understand the resolution and thamarah al-khilaf
The text suggests the dispute is verbal and reduces to one's stance on ta'thir vs. munasabah. The practical effect is seen in cases like qiyas of intoxication on slander for hadd, and qiyas of apostasy on theft for execution.
The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) among Hanafis is permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة: هل يجري القياس في العلل والشروط لا خلاف في أنه لا تثبت العلل
وأوصافها كعلية الجنسية في ربا النساء وصفة السوم في نصاب الزكاة ولا الشروط وأوصافها، كاشتراط الشهود في النكاح وذكورتها مثلاً، ولا الأحكام وأوصافها، كجواز البتيراء ووجوب الوتر ابتداء من غير نص مقيس عليه، فإنّ هذا نصب الشرع بالرأي من غير حجة شرعية، بل إنما أمر القياس تعدية حكم أصل إلى مسكوت بجامع، ثم اختلفوا هل تصح هذه التعدية في العلل والشروط والأسباب بأن توجد علة أو سبب أو شرط لحكم لأجل مناط، فيقاس ما يوجد فيه المناط عليها، ويحكم بعليتها وبسببيتها وشرطيتها فكثير من الحنفية ومنهم الإمام فخر الإسلام والشافعية نعم يجوز وكثير قالوا : لا يجوز واختاره ابن الحاجب المالكي. قال الكشف: وعليه عامة أصحابنا فيما أظن والذي يدل على أن هذا الحبر الهمام أعني فخر الإسلام على الجواز قوله بعد إبانة أن هذه الأمور لا تثبت بالقياس وإنما أنكرنا هذه الجملة إذا لم يوجد له في الشريعة أصل يصح تعليله، فأما إذا وجد فلا بأس به. المنكرون قالوا: إن استقل الجامع فهو العلة إن كان مضبوطاً وإلا فمظنته وكل من الأصل والفرع من أفراده. وكذا الحال في الشرط، وأنت لا يذهب عليك أنه يجوز أن لا يكون المناط علة لأصل الحكم وإن كان مضبوطاً، بل إنما هو مناط لعلية العلة وشرطية الشرط، فلا يلزم من وجوده في الفرع إلاّ كونه علة أو شرطاً، لا أن يكون من أفراد العلة فافهم ودليل المجوزين أن العلية والسببية والشرطية أحكام من أحكام الله تعالى كالوجوب والندب وغير ذلك، فتخصيص القياس ببعض الأحكام دون بعض تحكم كيف والأمر بالاعتبار، وكذا عمل الصحابة غير مختص بصورة دون صورة أما تذكر قول أمير المؤمنين علي الأمير المؤمنين عمر كيف قاس سببية سببية شيء لحكم بالقياس على ما هو سبب لذلك الحكم، والمانع إنما يمنع قياس سببية شيء لحكم على سببية آخر لحكم آخر، ولم يوجد لهذا التمحل أثر في كلماتهم وبعضهم قالوا الخلاف إنما هو في المستنبطة دون المنصوصة، قال المصنف والحق أنه أي هذا المختلف فيه كالمتفق عليه في اشتراط التأثير أو كفاية المناسبة أو تجويز الإرسال فمن شرط التأثير في التعليل لأحكام شرط ههنا أيضاً، ومن اكتفى بما عداه فيها اكتفى ههنا أيضاً لأن الفرق بينهما تحكم فإن المسلك مسلك على كل تقدير إلا أنه لا إلحاق على الآخيرين لاستقلال المسلك فإنه حينئذ لا بد في المقيس من مناسبة يكون بها علة من غير حاجة إلى أمر آخر كالتأثير وغيره فلا يحتاج إلى أصل يلحق به فافهم. ومثال ذلك أي القياس في الأسباب ونحوها قياس أمير المؤمنين علي السكر على القذف بجامع الافتراء، وقياس الردة على السرقة الكبرى للحكمة الضرورية فالأول فيه هتك الدين، والثاني فيه هتك المال وإلى كل منهما حاجة ضرورية وأما المثقل أي قياسه على المحدد للقصاص بجامع القتل العمد العدوان والأكل أي قياسه على الوقاع للكفارة لكونه جناية
عن صوم الشهر المبارك مثله فليس منه لأن القياس على السبب عبارة عن أن يثبت عليه علة قياساً على علية أخرى لذلك الحكم أو لغيره، فلا بد هناك من وصفين: أحدهما أصل والآخر فرع، وههنا العلة أمر واحد وهو القتل العمد، العدوان والجناية الكاملة على الصوم، لكن الخلاف إنما كان في تحققهما في القتل بالمثقل والأكل عمداً أم لا، بل هذا تعميم النص بتحقيق المناط فتأمل.
Question: Does qiyas apply to causes and conditions? There is no disagreement that causes and their attributes are not established [by qiyas], such as the genus cause in usury of women and the attribute of grazing in the zakat threshold, nor conditions and their attributes like stipulating witnesses in marriage and their being male, nor rulings and their attributes like the permissibility of divorce by triple pronouncement and the obligation of witr based on no text measured against. This would be legislating by opinion without legal evidence. Rather qiyas is only the extension of a ruling from an original to a silent case via a commonality. Then they differed: is this extension valid in causes, conditions, and reasons? Many Hanafis, including Imam Fakhr al-Islam, and Shafi'is say yes, it is permissible. Many said no, and Ibn al-Hajib al-Maliki chose this. Al-Kashshaf said: the majority of our scholars are on this [permissibility] as I think. Evidence for the permissibility view: these are rulings like obligation etc., and the practice of the Companions was not restricted; remember when Ali and Umar measured the causality of drinking on the causality of slander. The deniers said... etc.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut discusses the dispute over whether qiyas can be used to establish effective causes (illal), conditions (shurut), and reasons (asbab). The author first clarifies that there is no dispute that causes themselves cannot be invented by qiyas; the issue is whether qiyas can be used to prove that something is a cause, condition, or reason for a ruling. The majority of Hanafis, including Fakhr al-Islam, allow it, as do the Shafi'is. Others, including some Hanafis and Ibn al-Hajib, forbid it. The author presents arguments from both sides: the deniers argue that the commonality (jami') must be precisely defined and part of the cause's class; the permissibilists argue that causehood is a divine ruling like any other and thus subject to qiyas, as shown by the Companions' practices. The author then shows that the dispute reduces to one's position on talil: those who require ta'thir (effective attribute) in the original will require it here, while those who are satisfied with munasabah (suitability) will allow it here as well. Examples follow, including Ali's qiyas of intoxication on slander due to shared iftira' (falsehood), and the qiyas of apostasy on theft due to a pressing need. The author notes that the dispute is essentially verbal and that many scholars do not hesitate to use qiyas on causes in practice.

Key Terms
علة (illah): The effective cause that brings about a ruling
سبب (sabab): A reason that leads to a ruling, similar to illah but often external
شرط (shart): A condition necessary for the ruling's application
قياس (qiyas): Extending a ruling from an original case to a new case due to shared cause

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) He allows it.
C) He is silent.
D) He considers it invalid from the start.

Key Takeaway
Many Hanafis permit qiyas to establish causes, conditions, and reasons, following the practice of the Companions and considering causehood as a divine ruling subject to analogy.

Shafi'i Classification of Qiyas by Strength
Definition and example of Shafi'i jali and khafi qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Shafi'i qiyas jali and khafi based on knowledge of elimination of difference, and identify the three subdivisions of jali qiyas.

Core Idea
Shafi'i jali qiyas requires certain knowledge that the distinguishing factor is irrelevant; khafi qiyas relies on conjecture.

This lesson introduces the Shafi'i classification of qiyas by strength. The Hanafi school uses a different criterion, but understanding this Shafi'i division is crucial for grasping their usul framework. We will examine the definitions, examples, and subdivisions of clear (jali) and hidden (khafi) qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i criterion
Read the first sentence: 'عند الشافعية فباعتبار القوة ينقسم إلى قياس جلي وخفي'. The criterion is 'strength' of the evidence. What does 'strength' mean here? It refers to whether the elimination of the distinguishing factor is known or not.
The text immediately defines jali as 'ما علم فيه إلغاء الفارق' – where the difference is known to be irrelevant.
2
Analyze the example of the female slave
The hadith about partial manumission of a slave is used to illustrate jali qiyas: comparing a female slave to a male slave. The gender difference is obviously irrelevant because the ruling is based on the decrease of ownership, not masculinity.
The text notes that this example is actually 'دلالة نص' (indication of a text) rather than pure qiyas, but it serves as an example.
3
Understand the subdivisions of jali qiyas
The text then divides jali qiyas into three types: (1) qiyas of the superior (الأولى) like hitting over saying 'uff'; (2) qiyas of the clear equal (الواضح المساوي) like burning property over eating it; (3) the lower hidden (الخفي الأدنى) which is actually a kind of khafi qiyas, like qiyas of apples on wheat for riba.
This third type is called 'adna' (lower) and is a subset of khafi qiyas.
4
Contrast with khafi qiyas
Khafi qiyas is defined as 'ما لم يعلم فيه إلغاء الفارق' – where elimination of the difference is not known. The utmost is conjecture (ظن), and therefore it is disputed.
Some scholars reject acting upon khafi qiyas, while jali is agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عدها لما ورد به (تقسيمات للقياس أما عند الشافعية فباعتبار القوة) ينقسم (إلى) قياس (جلي، وهو ما علم فيه إلغاء، الفارق كالأمة على العبد في حق التقويم على معتق (البعض) قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من أعتق شركاً له في عبد وكان له مال يبلغ به ثمن العبد قوم العبد عليه قيمة عدل، فأعطى شركاءه حصصهم وعتق عليه العبد وإلا فقد عتق ما عتق رواه البخاري. وظاهر أن خصوصية الذكورة ملغاة. وإنما التقويم لتنقيص ملكه وخروج العبد من أن يتصرف فيه سيد بعضه أن يبيع، والأمة فيه مساوية للعبد، فيتعدى الحكم وينفي الفارق والحق أن هذا دلالة نص، فمن من القياس يكون هذا قياساً وإلا لا (والى) قياس (خفي بخلافه) أي ما لم يعلم فيه إلغاء الفارق وإنما قصارى الأمر الظن (ولذلك اختلف فيه فنفى التعبد به. وأما الجلي فهو متفق عليه بين الأنام (وقيل) القياس (الجلي قياس الأولى بالحكم على غيره كالضرب على التأفيف) في التحريم فإن الأول أولى بالحرمة من الثاني (و) قياس الواضح المساوي) بحيث لا ينبغي أن يشك فيه كإحراق مال اليتيم على أكله فإن كليهما متساويان في التلف المحرم (والخفي الأدنى) أي قياس الأدنى على الأعلى ( كالتفاح) أي قياسه (على البر) في حرمة الربا . (و) ينقسم (باعتبار العلة إلى قياس علة ما صرح فيه بها كقولهم : التفاح مطعوم، فيجري فيه الربا كالبر (وإلى قياس دلالة ما لم تذكر فيه العلة صريحاً و(دل عليها بملازمها كقطع الجماعة بالواحد) أي كقياسه على قتلهم (به أي بالواحد الثابت بإجماع الصحابة (بجامع وجوب الدية) فإن الدية واجبة فيهما إذا كانا خطأين (وهو) دليل القصاص فعلم من وجوب الدية وجوب القصاص (لأنهما) أي وجوب الدية ووجوب القصاص موجبان (متلازمان) فيما بينهما (للجناية) العلة لهما، فإذا علم وجوب الدية فيهما على وجود الجناية لأنها العلة وحدها، ووجود ما وجب به القصاص، فالمذكور لازم العلة لا العلة نفسها وإلى قياس في معنى الأصل وهو ما لا يجمع بين الأصل والفرع (إلا) بنفي الفارق ولو كان (ظنياً) ولا يحتاج إلى أمر آخر (كإلغاء كون المفطر جماعاً في إيجاب الكفارة فإنها تستدعي الجناية والذنب، لأنها كاسمها ستارة، وخصوص الجماع لا دخل له في الجناية الذنب، وإنما هي إفطار الصوم عمداً فتجب الكفارة بعمد الأكل أيضاً وأما عند الحنفية فباعتبار التبادر إليه قسموا (إلى) قياس (جلي) وهو ما يتبادر إليه الذهن في أول الأمر (و) إلى قياس (خفي منه وهو ما لا يتبادر إليه الذهن إلا بعد التأمل والثاني الاستحسان بالمعنى الأخص وكثيراً ما يراد به في الفقه هذا المعنى (وقد يقال : لكل دليل في مقابلة القياس الظاهر نص) من كتاب أو سنة (كالسلم) أي كنصه. وهو الآية والحديث اللذان تقدما، ولهذا قال الإمام: إنا أثبتنا الرجم بالاستحسان على خلاف
Count them as they are reported. Divisions of qiyas: According to the Shafi'is, by strength, it is divided into clear qiyas (jali) which is where the distinguishing factor is known to be eliminated, like the female slave compared to the male slave in the hadith of manumission: The Prophet said: 'Whoever frees a share in a slave and has sufficient wealth, the slave is evaluated at a fair price, then he gives his partners their shares, and the slave is freed; otherwise he is freed as much as he is freed.' (Bukhari). It is apparent that the attribute of masculinity is irrelevant. Rather, the valuation is due to the decrease of his ownership and the slave emerging from being under the control of a partial owner to being free. The female slave is equal to the male in this, so the ruling is extended and the difference is negated. In reality, this is an indication of the text, so is this qiyas or not? And to hidden qiyas (khafi), the opposite: where the elimination of the difference is not known, and the utmost is conjecture. Therefore it is disputed and some deny acting upon it. As for clear qiyas, it is agreed upon by all. And it was said: clear qiyas is qiyas of the superior in ruling over others, like hitting over saying 'uff' in prohibition, for the first is more deserving of prohibition than the second. And qiyas of the clear equal where no doubt should exist, like burning the orphan's property over consuming it, for both are equal in causing destruction. And the lower hidden (al-khafi al-adna) is qiyas of the lower on the higher, like qiyas of apples on wheat for riba prohibition. And it is divided by cause into qiyas 'illah where the cause is explicitly stated, like 'apple is edible' so riba applies as in wheat, and into qiyas dalalah where the cause is not explicitly stated but indicated by its concomitant, like qiyas of killing a group by one person on killing one person via the commonality of the necessity of blood-money, for blood-money is wajib in both if they were accidental. And the necessity of blood-money indicates the necessity of retaliation because they are concomitant for the crime. So the mentioned is the necessary of the cause, not the cause itself. And to qiyas fi ma'na al-asl, which does not combine original and branch except by negation of difference, even if conjectural, and needs no other element, like negating that the nullifier is intercourse in requiring kaffarah, for kaffarah requires transgression and sin because it is a cover, and the specificity of intercourse is not relevant to transgression; rather it is intentional breaking of the fast, so kaffarah becomes obligatory by intentional eating as well. And according to the Hanafis, by immediate mental understanding, they divided into clear qiyas (jali) which comes to mind first, and hidden qiyas (khafi) which does not come to mind except after reflection. The second is istihsan in the specific sense, and often used in fiqh with this meaning. And it is said: every evidence in opposition to apparent qiyas is a text from Book or Sunnah, like the salam contract which is a text; that is the verse and hadith mentioned earlier. Hence the Imam said: We established stoning by istihsan contrary to qiyas.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage from Fawatih al-Rahmut presents the various divisions of qiyas. It begins with the Shafi'i classification by strength: clear qiyas (jali), where the distinguishing factor is known to be irrelevant, exemplified by comparing a female slave to a male slave for the ruling of valuation upon partial manumission, based on the hadith of manumission. The text notes that this is actually an indication of the text (dalalah al-nass) rather than pure qiyas. Hidden qiyas (khafi) is the opposite. Then the Shafi'i subdivision: jali is further divided into qiyas of the superior (like hitting over saying 'uff'), qiyas of the equal (like burning property), and the lower hidden (qiyas of the lower on the higher, like apples on wheat for riba). Then qiyas is divided by cause into qiyas 'illah (cause explicitly stated) and qiyas dalalah (cause inferred from a concomitant, e.g., from wajib al-diyah we infer wajib al-qisas because they are necessary concomitants of the crime). Also qiyas fi ma'na al-asl (qiyas in the meaning of the original) which relies purely on negation of difference, like the kaffarah for eating being the same as for intercourse. Finally, the Hanafi division: by immediate mental understanding—jali (immediately understood) and khafi (requires reflection), and the khafi is identified as istihsan in the specific sense. The passage ends with a note that any evidence opposing apparent qiyas is actually a text from Quran or Sunnah, as exemplified by the salam contract and the ruling of stoning established by istihsan.

Key Terms
قياس جلي (qiyas jali): Clear qiyas where the distinguishing factor is known to be irrelevant (Shafi'i) or immediately understood (Hanafi)
قياس خفي (qiyas khafi): Hidden qiyas where the elimination of difference is not known (Shafi'i) or requires reflection (Hanafi)
إلغاء الفارق (ilgha al-fariq): Elimination of the distinguishing factor; considering it irrelevant to the ruling.
قياس الأولى (qiyas al-awla): Qiyas of the superior; where the branch is more deserving of the ruling than the original.
خفي أدنى (khafi adna): Lower hidden; qiyas of the lower on the higher, where the branch is less deserving.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Shafi'i classification, which of the following is an example of qiyas jali?
A) Qiyas of apples on wheat for riba
B) Qiyas of hitting on saying 'uff'
C) Qiyas of a female slave on a male slave for valuation
D) Qiyas of burning property on consuming it

Key Takeaway
Shafi'i jali qiyas is defined by the certain knowledge that the distinguishing factor is irrelevant, agreed upon by all, while khafi qiyas is conjectural and disputed.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
10 min
Divisions of Qiyas: Jali and Khafi
Explaining divisions of qiyas by strength and by 'illa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between qiyas jali and qiyas khafi according to both Hanafi and Shafi'i schools and identify the underlying usul principle.

Core Idea
The definition of qiyas jali differs: Hanafis prioritize immediate appearance; Shafi'is require known elimination of the distinguishing factor.

Qiyas (analogical reasoning) is a key source of Islamic law, but not all analogies are equal. This lesson explores the classification of qiyas into clear (jali) and hidden (khafi), showing how the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools define these categories differently. Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly applying qiyas and recognizing when istihsan (juristic preference) may override it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main divisions
The text first presents the Shafi'i division by strength: jali (clear) where the distinguishing factor is known to be eliminated, and khafi (hidden) where it is not. Then the Hanafi division by immediate appearance: jali comes to mind first, khafi requires reflection.
Shafi'is focus on epistemological certainty; Hanafis on cognitive immediacy.
2
Analyze the example of the slave girl
The hadith about partial emancipation mentions a male slave. The ruling is extended to a female slave because masculinity is an irrelevant distinction. The passage notes that this is actually dalaalat al-nass (indication of the text) rather than qiyas, highlighting the borderline between text-based extension and analogy.
This example is used to illustrate jali qiyas in the Shafi'i sense.
3
Examine the sub-categories of qiyas by strength and by 'illa
The text mentions qiyas al-awla (priority, e.g., beating over scolding), qiyas al-musawi (equal, e.g., burning orphan's property over eating it), qiyas al-adna (inferior, e.g., apples to wheat). It also divides by 'illa: explicit 'illa (qiyas 'illa) and implicit (qiyas dalalah).
These classifications refine the concept of jali and khafi.
4
Understand the Hanafi equation of qiyas khafi with istihsan
For Hanafis, qiyas khafi is often considered istihsan in the specific sense. The text gives examples: stoning established by istihsan contrary to qiyas (actually a text) and istisna' (contract of manufacture) based on consensus.
This explains why Hanafis accept istihsan as a source while Shafi'is generally reject it.
5
Compare the two schools' approaches
Both schools agree on jali qiyas as a binding proof, but differ on khafi. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that Shafi'is may restrict analogies more strictly, while Hanafis use istihsan to relax rigid analogies when a text, consensus, or necessity supports a different ruling.
The disagreement does not affect everyday fiqh in most cases but appears in contested areas like stoning and business contracts.

Source Text

الأصل الرابع/ القياس
عن صوم الشهر المبارك مثله فليس منه لأن القياس على السبب عبارة عن أن يثبت عليه علة قياساً على علية أخرى لذلك الحكم أو لغيره، فلا بد هناك من وصفين: أحدهما أصل والآخر فرع، وههنا العلة أمر واحد وهو القتل العمد، العدوان والجناية الكاملة على الصوم، لكن الخلاف إنما كان في تحققهما في القتل بالمثقل والأكل عمداً أم لا، بل هذا تعميم النص بتحقيق المناط (فتأمل).
عدها لما ورد به (تقسيمات للقياس أما عند الشافعية فباعتبار القوة) ينقسم (إلى) قياس (جلي، وهو ما علم فيه إلغاء، الفارق كالأمة على العبد في حق التقويم على معتق (البعض) قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم : من أعتق شركاً له في عبد وكان له مال يبلغ به ثمن العبد قوم العبد عليه قيمة عدل، فأعطى شركاءه حصصهم وعتق عليه العبد وإلا فقد عتق ما عتق رواه البخاري. وظاهر أن خصوصية الذكورة ملغاة. وإنما التقويم لتنقيص ملكه وخروج العبد من أن يتصرف فيه سيد بعضه أن يبيع، والأمة فيه مساوية للعبد، فيتعدى الحكم وينفي الفارق والحق أن هذا دلالة نص، فمن من القياس يكون هذا قياساً وإلا لا (والى) قياس (خفي بخلافه) أي ما لم يعلم فيه إلغاء الفارق وإنما قصارى الأمر الظن (ولذلك اختلف فيه فنفى التعبد به. وأما الجلي فهو متفق عليه بين الأنام (وقيل) القياس (الجلي قياس الأولى بالحكم على غيره كالضرب على التأفيف) في التحريم فإن الأول أولى بالحرمة من الثاني (و) قياس الواضح المساوي) بحيث لا ينبغي أن يشك فيه كإحراق مال اليتيم على أكله فإن كليهما متساويان في التلف المحرم (والخفي الأدنى) أي قياس الأدنى على الأعلى ( كالتفاح) أي قياسه (على البر) في حرمة الربا . (و) ينقسم (باعتبار العلة إلى قياس علة ما صرح فيه بها كقولهم : التفاح مطعوم، فيجري فيه الربا كالبر (وإلى قياس دلالة ما لم تذكر فيه العلة صريحاً و(دل عليها بملازمها كقطع الجماعة بالواحد) أي كقياسه على قتلهم (به أي بالواحد الثابت بإجماع الصحابة (بجامع وجوب الدية) فإن الدية واجبة فيهما إذا كانا خطأين (وهو) دليل القصاص فعلم من وجوب الدية وجوب القصاص (لأنهما) أي وجوب الدية ووجوب القصاص موجبان (متلازمان) فيما بينهما (للجناية) العلة لهما، فإذا علم وجوب الدية فيهما على وجود الجناية لأنها العلة وحدها، ووجود ما وجب به القصاص، فالمذكور لازم العلة لا العلة نفسها وإلى قياس في معنى الأصل وهو ما لا يجمع بين الأصل والفرع (إلا) بنفي الفارق ولو كان (ظنياً) ولا يحتاج إلى أمر آخر (كإلغاء كون المفطر جماعاً في إيجاب الكفارة فإنها تستدعي الجناية والذنب، لأنها كاسمها ستارة، وخصوص الجماع لا دخل له في الجناية الذنب، وإنما هي إفطار الصوم عمداً فتجب الكفارة بعمد الأكل أيضاً وأما عند الحنفية فباعتبار التبادر إليه قسموا (إلى) قياس (جلي) وهو ما يتبادر إلى الذهن في أول الأمر (و) إلى قياس (خفي منه وهو ما لا يتبادر إلى الذهن إلا بعد التأمل والثاني الاستحسان بالمعنى الأخص وكثيراً ما يراد به في الفقه هذا المعنى (وقد يقال : لكل دليل في مقابلة القياس الظاهر نص) من كتاب أو سنة (كالسلم) أي كنصه. وهو الآية والحديث اللذان تقدما، ولهذا قال الإمام: إنا أثبتنا الرجم بالاستحسان على خلاف القياس والمراد به نص الرجم فاندفع إيراد الرازي الشافعي أن هذا الاستحسان إن كان قياساً فقد أثبتم الحد به، وإلا فلا يكون حجة أصلاً أو إجماع كالاستصناع صورته أن يقول للخراز أخرزني خفاً بقيمة كذا من جلد كذا وقدر كذا وهذا ينعقد عندنا بيعاً لا عدة، مع أن القياس يأبى عنه لعدم المبيح إلا أنه انعقد الإجماع على جوازه في الصدر: الأول لأنهم كانوا يتعاملون به من غير نكير أو ضرورة ، كطهارة الحياض والآبار بعد تنجسهما والقياس يقتضي أن لا تطهر أبداً لبقاء الماء النجس ولو قليلاً، وكذا أرضه نجس لم يستعمل في المطهر إلا أنه حكم بالطهار للضرورة والوقوع في الحرج العظيم، ثم هذه الضرورة إما راجعة إلى الإجماع والضرورة مستندة، أو إلى القياس الخفي فافهم.
The fourth principle: Qiyas. For example, the fast of the blessed month is not like it because analogy on the cause means establishing an 'illa on it by analogy to another 'illa for that ruling or another; thus two attributes are needed: one is the original and the other is the branch. Here the 'illa is one thing: intentional killing, aggression and complete transgression against the fast, but the disagreement was only in whether they are realized in killing with a blunt instrument and eating intentionally or not; rather this is generalization of the text by verification of the basis (so reflect). Its divisions according to the Shafi'is by strength: it is divided into clear analogy (jali) which is where elimination of the distinguishing factor is known, like the slave girl to the slave in the right of valuation upon the one who frees a part. The Messenger of Allah said: Whoever frees his share in a slave and has wealth that reaches the price of the slave, the slave is valued for him at a fair value, then he gives the partners their shares and the slave is free to him; otherwise what is freed is freed. Reported by Bukhari. It is apparent that the particularity of masculinity is eliminated. Valuation is for the reduction of his ownership and the slave's exit from being disposed of by the owner of a part to sell, and the slave girl is equal to the slave in that, so the ruling extends and the distinguishing factor is negated. The truth is that this is the indication of the text, so whoever considers this analogy or not. And to hidden analogy (khafi) opposite to it, i.e. where elimination of the distinguishing factor is not known, and the utmost is probability. Therefore they differed about it: some denied acting upon it. As for clear analogy, it is agreed upon among the people. And it was said: clear analogy is the analogy of the priority of the ruling over another, like beating over scolding in prohibition, for the former is more deserving of prohibition than the latter. And the obvious equal analogy such that there should be no doubt about it, like burning the orphan's property over eating it, for both are equal in prohibited destruction. And the inferior hidden analogy, i.e. analogy of the lower to the higher, like apples to wheat in the prohibition of riba. And it is divided by the 'illa into qiyas 'illa where the 'illa is explicitly mentioned, like their saying: apples are edible so riba applies to it like wheat. And into qiyas dalalah where the 'illa is not explicitly mentioned but is indicated by its concomitant, like killing a group by one person, i.e. analogy on killing them by one person established by the consensus of the Companions, based on the commonality of the obligation of blood money, for blood money is obligatory in both if they were accidental. And it is the evidence for retaliation, so from the obligation of blood money the obligation of retaliation is known because they are necessary concomitants with respect to the injury, the 'illa for both. So when the obligation of blood money is known for both for the existence of injury because it is the sole 'illa, and the existence of what necessitates retaliation is known, then the mentioned is a necessary concomitant of the 'illa, not the 'illa itself. And to qiyas fi ma'na al-asl, which is what does not combine the original and the branch except by negating the distinguishing factor even if it is probable and does not need another matter, like eliminating that the break-fast act is sexual intercourse in the obligation of expiation, for it requires injury and sin, because it is like a cover, and the particularity of intercourse has no role in the injury and sin; it is only the intentional breaking of the fast, so expiation is also obligatory for intentional eating. As for the Hanafis, they divided it by immediate appearance into clear analogy (jali) which comes to mind first, and hidden analogy (khafi) which does not come to mind except after reflection. The second is istihsan in the specific sense, and frequently in fiqh it is meant by this. And it may be said: every proof in opposition to apparent analogy is a text from Book or Sunnah, like salam, i.e. like its text. It is the verse and hadith that preceded, and therefore the Imam said: We established stoning by istihsan contrary to qiyas, and what is meant is the text of stoning, so the objection of al-Razi al-Shafi'i is repelled that if this istihsan were qiyas, then you have established the hadd by it, otherwise it is not a proof at all; or it is consensus like istisna'. Its form is that one says to the leatherworker: Make me a khuff for such a price from such leather and such amount, and this is concluded with us as a sale, not a contract, even though qiyas refuses it due to lack of permissibility, except that consensus was established on its permissibility in the early period because they used to deal with it without objection, or necessity, like purification of water basins and wells after their contamination, and qiyas requires that they never become pure due to the remaining impure water even if little, and similarly its earth is impure and not used for purification, but purity was judged due to necessity and falling into great hardship. Then this necessity either refers to consensus and necessity is based, or to hidden analogy, so understand.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage defines and categorizes qiyas (analogical reasoning). It begins by noting that qiyas requires two attributes: one as an original (asl) and one as a branch (far'). It then presents the Shafi'i division based on strength into jali (clear) and khafi (hidden), with examples. For jali, the example of a slave girl analogous to a slave in valuation upon partial emancipation is given, citing the hadith of the Prophet. It explains that the particularity of masculinity is irrelevant, thus the ruling extends. For khafi, it is based on probability. Then it presents alternative classifications: qiyas al-awla (priority), qiyas al-musawi (equal), qiyas al-adna (inferior). It also divides by 'illa into qiyas 'illa (explicit 'illa) and qiyas dalalah (implicit 'illa). Finally, it gives the Hanafi division based on immediate appearance (jali and khafi). The end of the passage discusses istihsan as a proof opposing qiyas, with examples of stoning and istisna'.

Key Terms
القياس الجلي (al-qiyas al-jali): Analogy where the distinguishing factor (fariq) is known to be eliminated (Shafi'i) or which immediately comes to mind (Hanafi).
القياس الخفي (al-qiyas al-khafi): Analogy where elimination of fariq is not known (Shafi'i) or which requires reflection (Hanafi); often equated with istihsan by Hanafis.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A proof that opposes qiyas, either another qiyas, text, consensus, or necessity.
دلالة النص (dalaalat al-nass): The indication of the text itself, stronger than qiyas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which school defines qiyas jali as 'what immediately comes to mind'?
A) Shafi'i school
B) Hanafi school
C) Maliki school
D) Hanbali school

Key Takeaway
Qiyas jali is unanimously accepted as a proof, but its definition differs between Hanafis (immediate appearance) and Shafi'is (known elimination of fariq), with practical implications for when istihsan may apply.

Al-Qiyas — Analogical Reasoning
intermediate
6 min
Classification of Qiyas and Istihsan with the Example of Predatory Bird Saliva
Classification and application of usul rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify qiyas and istihsan based on the strength of their effect and the hiddenness of their correctness, and apply the Hanafi preference rules to derive a ruling in a novel case.

Core Idea
Strong-effect istihsan trumps weak-effect qiyas; hidden-correct qiyas trumps hidden-corrupt istihsan.

This passage from Fawatih al-Rahamut presents a nuanced classification of qiyas and istihsan. Rather than treating them as absolute categories, Hanafi usul scholars evaluate the strength and hiddenness of their effects and underlying reasons. The example of predatory bird saliva demonstrates how these preferences play out in practice, leading to a ruling that differs from apparent qiyas.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two-fold division of istihsan and qiyas
The text divides istihsan into one with strong effect (no hidden corruption) and one with hidden corruption. Qiyas is divided into one with weak effect and one with hidden correctness. Understand each category.
Istihsan with strong effect: its correctness is apparent. Qiyas with weak effect: its corruption is known by reflection.
2
State the preference rule
The first of the first (strong istihsan) is preferred over the first of the second (weak qiyas). The second of the second (hidden-correct qiyas) is preferred over the second of the first (hidden-corrupt istihsan).
This prioritises both types: strong istihsan over weak qiyas, and hidden-correct qiyas over hidden-corrupt istihsan.
3
Apply the rule to the example of predatory bird saliva
By qiyas to predatory land beasts, the saliva is impure (weak qiyas). By istihsan based on similarity to humans (pure), it is pure (strong istihsan). According to the rule, the strong istihsan prevails, so the saliva is ruled pure.
The cause (illa) of the qiyas is the mixing of impure moisture, which is absent in birds.
4
Analyse the cause (illa) of the qiyas
The qiyas's cause is 'mixing with impure moisture' from saliva. Birds drink with their beaks (bone, pure), so water does not mix with saliva. The cause is absent, weakening the qiyas.
The absence of the cause makes the qiyas 'weak in effect'.
5
Evaluate the final ruling with doubt
Although the primary ruling is purity by istihsan, due to doubt about beak contamination from carrion, the water is deemed makruh (disliked) if other water is available. This shows the application of preference rules alongside caution.
The ruling is not absolute purity; tanzihan makruh indicates the preferred nature of istihsan over qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قسموا الاستحسان إلى ما قوي أثره بأن لم يكن فيه فساد خفي وإلى ما ظهر (صحته في بادىء الرأي وإن كان هذا الظاهر خفياً بالنسبة إلى القياس وخفي فساده) يعرف بالتأمل (و) قسموا (القياس إلى ما ضعف أثره) بأن يعرف بالتأمل فساده وإلى ما ظهر فساده) في بادىء الرأي وخفي صحته، وذلك بأن ينضم إليه معنى يفيده قوة فأول الأول وهو الاستحسان الذي قوي أثره (مقدم على أول الثاني) وهو القياس الضعيف الأثر (وثاني الثاني وهو القياس الخفي الصحة مقدم (على ثاني وهو الاستحسان الخفي الفساد وهذا ظاهر فالأول كسور سباع الطير) فإنه (نجس قياساً على سور سباع البهائم، لأن السؤر معتبر باللحم ولحمها حرام نجس (وطاهر استحساناً كسور الآدمي فالقياس عليه جيد من القياس الأول وإن كان هو أظهر وذلك لضعف علة القياس، وهو) أي علة القياس والتذكير باعتبار تأويلها بالوصف الجامع (مخالطة الرطوبة النجسة) في السؤر، ولا توجد هذه العلة في سباع الطيور إذ تشرب بمنقارها) فيخالط الماء دون اللعاب (وهو عظم طاهر) فما لاقى إلا طاهراً وملاقاة الطاهر لا توجب النجاسة (فكان كسور الآدمي، وهذا أقوى، لأن تأثير ملاقاة الطاهر في بقائه طاهراً أشد وأقوى قيل ما يقع منها أي من سباع الطيور على الجيف سوره نجس، لأن منقاره لا يخلو عن نجاسة عادة لأكله الجيف فيصير نجساً لمخالطة هذه النجاسة (وأجيب بأن عادتها ذلك المنقار بالأرض بعد الأكل منه (فيطهر) المنقار، نعم في شبهة بقاء أثر النجاسة، فلهذا أي شبهة وقوع أثر اللعاب فيه أيضاً حكم بكراهته عند وجود ماء آخر فتأمل
Then they divided istihsan into what has a strong effect, as in it there is no hidden corruption, and into what appears (its correctness in initial opinion, even if this appearance is hidden relative to qiyas, and its corruption is hidden) known by reflection. And they divided qiyas into what has a weak effect, known by reflection to be corrupt, and into what appears corrupt in initial opinion but its correctness is hidden, because a meaning joins it that gives it strength. So the first of the first, which is istihsan with strong effect, is preferred over the first of the second, which is qiyas with weak effect. And the second of the second, which is qiyas with hidden correctness, is preferred over the second, which is istihsan with hidden corruption. This is apparent. So the first (istihsan with strong effect) is like the saliva of predatory birds: it is impure by qiyas based on the saliva of predatory beasts, because saliva is considered by the meat and their meat is forbidden and impure. And it is pure by istihsan, like the saliva of humans. So the qiyas based on it is valid from the first qiyas, even though it is more apparent, because the cause of the qiyas is weak. The cause of the qiyas (and the masculine pronoun is by considering it as a comprehensive description) is the mixing of impure moisture in the saliva, and this cause is not present in predatory birds because they drink with their beaks, so the water mixes with the beak, not the saliva, and the beak is pure bone. So what touches it is only pure, and contact with a pure thing does not cause impurity. So it is like human saliva, and this is stronger because the effect of contact with a pure thing in remaining pure is more severe and strong. It is said: what falls from them (i.e., from predatory birds) on carrion, its saliva is impure because its beak is usually not free from impurity due to eating carrion, so it becomes impure due to mixing with this impurity. And it is answered: their habit is to rub the beak on the ground after eating, so the beak becomes pure. Yes, due to the doubt of remaining impurity, for this doubt of the trace of saliva also, it is ruled disliked (makruh) when other water is available. So consider.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
Passage type: Classification of qiyas and istihsan with an example. The text first divides istihsan and qiyas into categories based on the strength/weakness of their effect and the hiddenness/apparentness of their correctness or corruption. The rule: istihsan with strong effect is preferred over qiyas with weak effect; and qiyas with hidden correctness is preferred over istihsan with hidden corruption. The example of the saliva (sur) of predatory birds illustrates this: by qiyas to predatory land animals, it is impure, but by istihsan (analogy to humans) it is pure. The reasoning is that birds drink with their beak (bone, pure) not with their tongue/lips that mix saliva. So the cause (mixing with impure moisture) is absent. The objection about the beak being contaminated by carrion is answered by their habit of cleaning it. Ultimately, due to doubt, it is deemed makruh if other water exists.

Key Terms
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): A method of juristic preference that takes precedence over qiyas when the qiyas is weak in effect or has hidden corruption.
السؤر (al-su'r): The leftover water or saliva from an animal's mouth.
سباع الطير (siba' al-tayr): Predatory birds that hunt and eat carrion, such as hawks and eagles.
القياس الخفي (al-qiyas al-khafi): Qiyas whose correctness is hidden, appearing corrupt initially but proven correct upon deeper analysis.
العلة (al-'illa): The effective cause that grounds a qiyas ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the saliva of predatory birds ruled pure by istihsan?
A) Because all bird saliva is pure
B) Because they drink with their beaks which are pure bone, so the water does not mix with saliva
C) Because the qiyas to land predators is invalid
D) Because humans and birds are similar in all respects

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, strong-effect istihsan overrides weak-effect qiyas, and hidden-correct qiyas overrides hidden-corrupt istihsan, as demonstrated by the example of predatory bird saliva.

Sajdat al-Tilawa: Qiyas vs Istihsan in Action
Application of qiyas and istihsan to sajdat al-tilawa

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi usul concepts of qiyas and istihsan to analyze the ruling of sajdat al-tilawa, and distinguish between superficially correct and flawed reasoning.

Core Idea
For sajdat al-tilawa, qiyas suggests bowing suffices but is flawed; istihsan forbids it but is also flawed—only nuanced analysis resolves it.

This passage presents a classic illustration of how qiyas and istihsan are evaluated in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Using the example of the prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawa), the text shows that both a superficial qiyas and a seemingly stronger istihsan can be faulty. By carefully examining the purpose of the act and the nature of the commanded elements, the Hanafi school arrives at a balanced position. This lesson will walk you through the reasoning, helping you internalize the criteria for valid qiyas and the proper role of istihsan.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two competing arguments
The passage contrasts a qiyas (analogical argument) that performing sajdat al-tilawa by bowing (ruku') in prayer is sufficient, with an istihsan (juristic preference) that it is not allowed. The qiyas focuses on the common purpose (exaltation), while the istihsan relies on the analogy to prayer prostrations.
This is a typical usul scenario: a qiyas that seems plausible but is deemed weak, versus an istihsan that appears stronger but is later found flawed.
2
Analyze the qiyas argument
The qiyas argues: the purpose of sajdat al-tilawa is exaltation, and bowing also expresses exaltation; therefore, bowing can substitute. The passage notes that this qiyas is 'apparently corrupt' because it substitutes a different commanded act, and bowing is not commanded for this purpose. Also, it would allow overlapping (tadākhul) when multiple verses are recited.
The flaw is that the commanded act (prostration) is performed by something else (bowing) that is not specifically commanded. This violates the requirement that the commanded act be performed as commanded.
3
Analyze the istihsan argument
The istihsan (held by the three imams) says bowing does not substitute, based on analogy to prayer prostrations: in prayer, bowing does not fulfill the obligation of prostration. The common factor is that both prostration and bowing are individual acts of worship. The passage declares this istihsan 'inwardly corrupt' because in prayer bowing and prostration are each individually required by explicit command (Quran 22:77), so one cannot substitute for the other. But sajdat al-tilawa is not intrinsically intended; it is only a means of exaltation at the moment of recitation.
The difference between prayer prostrations and sajdat al-tilawa is critical: the latter is not an independent act of worship; it is a response to recitation, so its purpose can be achieved by bowing if the context permits.
4
Understand the exceptions and evidence
The text adds nuances: outside prayer, bowing is not a recognized devotional act, so it cannot substitute. If the verse is recited in the first rak'ah and not performed immediately, it becomes a debt (dīn) in the dhimmah, making it like a prayer prostration. Reports from Ibn Umar and Ibn Mas'ud indicate that they allowed either bowing or prostrating for sajdat al-tilawa in prayer, showing the permissibility.
These details show that the ruling is context-dependent, highlighting the sophistication of Hanafi istidlal.
5
Synthesize the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that sajdat al-tilawa can be performed by bowing in prayer (as an option), based on the stronger evidence from the companions and the refined analysis that the act's purpose (exaltation) can be achieved by bowing. The qiyas and istihsan are both partially flawed; the correct view emerges from a deeper understanding of the nature of the act.
This example illustrates that qiyas and istihsan are tools subject to critical evaluation, and the final ruling may incorporate elements of both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والثاني) وهو ما فيه القياس خفي الصحة دون الاستحسان كسجدة التلاوة القياس أن تؤدي بالركوع في الصلاة لظهور أن المقصود) من إيجاب هذا السجود (التعظيم) الله تعالى (مخالفة للمتكبرين) من المشركين (ولذا صح التداخل) فيها إذا قرئت آية أو سمعت مراراً في مجلس واحد (وهذا) القياس (فاسد ظاهر اللزوم تأدى المأمور به بغيره فإن الركوع ليس مأموراً به والاستحسان أن لا يجوز كما هو قول الأئمة الثلاثة قياساً على سجود الصلاة لا ينوب ركوعها عنه فكذا هذا والجامع كونه غير المأمور به (وهذا) الاستحسان (فاسد) باطناً، لأن كلاً من الركوع والسجود (مطلوب في الصلاة (بطلب يخصه) فيكون كل مطلوباً بالذات (قال) الله تعالى: أَرْكَعُواْ وَاسْجُدُوا ﴾ [الحج: ۷۷] (فامتنع تأدي أحدهما في ضمن الآخر وإلا فات مقصود الأمر بخلاف) سجدة التلاوة) فإنه غير مقصود، بالذات، وإنما التعظيم عند قراءة هذه الآيات. وهو كما يحصل بالسجود يحصل بالركوع، ولذا عبر في بعض آيات السجدة بالركوع، وإنما لم تتأدّ بالركوع خارج الصلاة لأن الركوع خارجها لم يعرف قربة، والتعظيم إنما يكون بما هو قربة عند الله تعالى وإنما لم تتأد بالركوع من ركعة سجدة آية قرئت في الأولى، لأنها لم تؤد في محلها صار ديناً في الذمة لازم القضاء في هذه الصلاة، فصار مقصوداً بالذات، فصارت كالصلاتية، فلا ينوب الركوع عنها، كذا قالوا. وفي «الحاشية» نقلاً عن التقرير عن ابن عمر أنه كان إذا قرأ النجم واقرأ باسم ربك في صلاة وبلغ آخرها كبر وركع، وإن قرأها في غير صلاة سجد. وعن ابن مسعود أنه سئل عن سجدة تكون في آخر السورة أيسجد لها أم يركع ؟ قال : إن شئت فاركع وإن شئت فاسجد ثم اقرأ بعدها سورة. وإن استدل بهذه الآثار فحسن
And the second: in which qiyas has hidden correctness while istihsan does not, like the prostration of recitation. The qiyas is that it is performed by bowing in prayer, because it is apparent that the purpose of making this prostration obligatory is exaltation of Allah Most High, in opposition to the arrogant polytheists. Hence, overlapping (tadākhul) is valid in it when an aya is recited or heard repeatedly in one gathering. This qiyas is apparently corrupt because the commanded act is performed by something else, for bowing is not commanded. And istihsan is that it is not allowed, as is the saying of the three imams, by analogy to the prostrations of prayer: bowing does not substitute for its prostration, so likewise here. The common factor is that it is not the commanded act. This istihsan is inwardly corrupt, because both bowing and prostration are required in prayer with a specific requirement, so each is intrinsically required. Allah Most High said: 'Bow and prostrate' (al-Hajj 77). So performing one in place of the other is prevented, otherwise the purpose of the command would be lost. Unlike the prostration of recitation, it is not intrinsically intended; rather, exaltation is intended when reciting these verses, and it is achieved by bowing as it is by prostration. Hence in some verses of prostration, it is expressed by bowing. It is not performed by bowing outside prayer because bowing outside it is not recognized as a devotional act, and exaltation is only through what is a devotional act to Allah. And it is not performed by bowing from a rak'ah if the prostration aya was recited in the first, because it was not performed in its place; it becomes a debt in the dhimmah, necessary to make up in this prayer, so it becomes intrinsically intended, thus it becomes like prayer prostrations, so bowing does not substitute for it. This is what they said. In the Hashiyah, it is reported from al-Taqrir from Ibn 'Umar that when he recited 'Najm' and 'Iqra' bismi rabbik' in prayer and reached the end, he said takbir and bowed. If he recited them outside prayer, he prostrated. And from Ibn Mas'ud, that he was asked about a prostration at the end of a surah: should he prostrate or bow? He said: If you wish, bow, and if you wish, prostrate, then recite another surah after it. If one uses these reports as evidence, it is good.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
Passage type: Application of the classification of qiyas and istihsan to the case of sajdat al-tilawa. The qiyas (performing it by bowing) is based on the purpose of exaltation, but it is considered apparently corrupt because it substitutes a different act. The istihsan (not allowing bowing) is based on analogy to prayer prostrations, but it is inwardly corrupt because bowing and prostration are both individually required in prayer, not so for recitation prostration where exaltation can be achieved by either. The text then explains the nuance: outside prayer, bowing is not a recognized act of worship; inside prayer, if the verse is recited in the first rak'ah and not performed there, it becomes a debt and thus like prayer prostrations. Reports from Ibn 'Umar and Ibn Mas'ud allow choice between bowing and prostrating for sajdat al-tilawa. The passage demonstrates the complexity of evaluating qiyas and istihsan.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawa): The prostration required upon reciting or hearing certain Quranic verses.
تداخل (tadākhul): Overlapping; in this context, the validity of performing multiple prostrations together when many verses are recited.
مقصود بالذات (maqsūd bi al-dhāt): Intrinsically intended; an act that is an end in itself, such as prayer prostrations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi analysis in the passage, why can sajdat al-tilawa be performed by bowing inside prayer?
A) Because bowing and prostrating are both pillars of prayer
B) Because the purpose is exaltation, which can be achieved by either
C) Because the Quran commands it
D) Because the three imams agree

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, a qiyas or istihsan may appear correct on the surface but can be invalidated by a deeper examination of the act's nature and purpose, as demonstrated by the case of sajdat al-tilawa.
